RATING: 7
Fun and fast card game. Split into two phases - the first phase is a draft phase where you must discern your opponents' strategies and decide your own. The second phase is an auction where you try and strengthen your position. There is some randomness but the game is so short that the randomness is fun rather than frustrating.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a great little fast game. It changes greatly from 2-4 players. I prefer 3-4 but 2 is very interesting as well. 

The theme does not shine through, but the art is beautiful and it helps make the game enjoyable. 

Game play is based around set collecting, but it is the placement and auction portions that really make the game shine. Choices are important, and determining what the really important cards to your hand to attain victory is a very sublime aspect.

Lots of game for little money. Love it.

RATING: 7
Interesting mechanic of drawing three cards, one at a time, and making a decision where to put the cards as drawn. A smidge of "press your luck" mixed with some strategic options for planning the endgame. All in all, a nice filler, but the cards are stiff, hard to shuffle, and smell horrid.

Card sleeves are mandatory for this title. With more plays, I expect to revise my rating -- most likely HIGHER, if I had to guess.

RATING: 8
20+ plays / 2,3,4 players

LIKE: Quick, very fun and competitive. Feels like a stock game more than an auction game. Love the partial-knowledge mechanism. Deeper game than it looks.
DISLIKE: Some randomness, so sometimes draws can be poor. Sometimes you can't tell what someone has. Theme is thin as paper.

OVERALL: It's a great game in a small package. Combines the stock feel with push-your luck and a bit of auction. Card counting is recommended, but not imperative. So many ways to trick people so you can slyly grab a different category majority. Great with 3 players, since you can try to get the other two players to compete for a category you don't want.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
It's common on BGG to say that a game has a 'pasted on' theme. Biblios is a fun, enjoyable game, with the character of Canasta (IMO ... bluffing, deception, guessing, leading to a big reveal), but much shorter and more random.

However, it literally has NOTHING to do with its theme. The mechanics, the win conditions, the style of gameplay, the interactions encouraged ... nothing. The theme is just an art direction. It's well-presented, but about as relevant as putting football players on Skip-Bo and calling it NFL, the Card Game. 

That presentation also serves to double the price.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
You would think that a theme about monks collecting different libraries of books wrapped in a brown box with a bald guy on it would be a good enough reason to make you want to play this game but wait, there's more! This is a really fun two phased set collection auction game where you spend the first phase allocating a series of cards into different regions (your hand, the flop for other players to draft from, and a deck that will be auctioned off in the second phase of the game) and the second phase bidding on the deck of cards created in the first. This leads to some really interesting dynamics reminiscent of games like for sale and modern art that keep me engaged in Biblios and the title in my collection. I still think that the "forbidden lore" library is the porn.

RATING: 7.5
This great filler surprised me a lot with the actual depth of gameplay that can offer. It's so simple... and yet there's so much with the bluffing, the foreseeing, the memory and the hand management! I love auction and here this mechanic works great and it's very intense.

The component are also great, the dice are awesome and the art is very nice. Yet what I enjoy the most about this game ist the satisfying feeling that comes, when I can foresee something or deduce what the other players might be doing. Biblios is my favourite filler card game at this point. I'm going to play it a lot!

RATING: 7.5
[30.08.2011]
Zu zweit sehr schön spielbar mit einem gewissen Unsicherheitsfaktor: Man weiß zwar, dass maximal 11 grüne/gelbe/rote, bzw. 25 braune/blaue Punkte im Spiel sein können; da aber 21 Karten am Anfang vom Spiel entfernt werden (plus 6 Geldkarten), ist nicht klar, wieviele Punkte man für eine Mehrheit braucht, und welche Karten man weggeben kann, um in der Auktionsphase Gold zu ersteigern.
Ausserdem wird durch das Entfernen der Karten die Spielzeit skaliert, was auch sinnvoll ist.

Schlisslich sehen die Karten schön aus, und die kleine Würfelablage zwischen den Spielern passt auch dazu.

Sehr gutes Reisespiel, findet Karin.

RATING: 5.5
It's OK: nothing more. The Church cards really don't make much of a difference to the final score; and really, although mildly entertaining, there just ain't all that much to Biblios. 

The comparisons with PAX (the far superior game) have me baffled. The only thing I see in common between the two is the card-drafting mechanism, which appears to have been lifted from the much, much better Reiner Knizia game, The Merchants of Amsterdam. In fact, Biblios feels very much like a Frankenstein's monster version of many a Knizia title.

Very nice looking, though, with a theme which has been lovingly pasted on.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Fun and clever filler with some interesting decisions.  Not exactly fireworks, but good for what it is.

Okay, the privately draw cards and decide whether to take a card, put the card in the phase 2 auction pile, or put it in the "available to the other players" array, is a fun central mechanic.  

One of my favorite fillers.  Giving it a 7.  April 2012.

This is a game that both gamers and non-gamers enjoy.  It is quick and pleasing for just about everyone.  Raising it to an 8. October 2014.

Putting this game into perspective, in particular, comparing it to all the other short games out there, considering how readily even non-gamers embrace it, Biblios deserves to be bumped up to a 9.  May 2016.

RATING: 6
Well designed, I enjoyed the two phases of the game and I think this is something my family would enjoy. It’s a good filler with seemingly interesting choices but ultimately felt too much like guess work for me. I’d need to play it more to get a better feel. The first phase was mainly pushing your luck to acquire the best card while seeding the auction deck and keeping half an eye on what your opponents are collecting. Having only a 1/3 knowledge of the auction deck in my 3 player game felt like too little knowledge to make any solid decisions or plans. For what it is though, a light filler card game it is fun and I wouldn’t turn my nose up at playing.

RATING: 8

RATING: 8
We shied away from Steve Finn games simply because they typically involved mechanisms we don't enjoy. This one especially as it has auctioning in it, one of our least favorite mechanisms. But after getting and really enjoying his "Cosmic Run" we decided to give this a try. And after getting it in a trade discovered that it really is a good little filler game. The game plays quick and easy. In the first half of the game players alternate drawing cards, keeping one, discarding another to a common deck then distributing the rest to other player(s). The strategy comes in knowing what to keep, what to discard and what to give your opponents. In the second half of the game you use the cards in your hand to auction for the cards that were discarded to the common pile earlier. So it becomes a very thinky game where you try and decide do you keep the gold to get better cards later or hold on to other cards to increase your chances of winning one of the dice that count towards your point total at the end of the game.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is the game I break out to teach new people what a fun modern game can be.

Biblios is the perfect marriage of great mechanics, push-your-luck card drafting, set collection and auctions.  They give the right mix of known and hidden information, enough signals to strategize while leaving room for small surprises and intentional misdirection.  There is still quite a bit of luck of the draw, but a great performance at auction is more than enough to make up for it.

It has engaged nearly everyone who I've played right from the first game.  Almost always ends up playing twice or more.  Plenty of post-game analysis from all players, a sure sign of a fun game.

Plays fast and wonderfully from 2 to 4 players in a small package.  What more could you ask for from a light game?  Superlative.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
Very original card game. It's goal is basically to get a point majority in the five card colors. In the first half of the game you draft the cards in a sort of push your luck way. In the second half of the game you bid on the cards. You can pay color cards with money cards, but you can also buy the money by discarding color cards that you don't (think) you need. This makes for pretty interesting decisions. Besides that you can also manipulate the value of the different colors. All in all a quick but challenging card game with a nice balance between luck and strategy.

Gameplay: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Replayability: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Fun/Social: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Components: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
Rules: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Looks pretty straightforward. You draw and decide cards to keep, give or auction until the deck is exhausted. Adjust category values whenever Bishops come up. You then auction the cards in the in the shuffled auction pile one by one, spending gold on workers and resources, spending numbers of cards on gold. Again, adjusting category values whenever Bishops come up. After auction, player with highest points in each category takes the die. Tie breaker is letter closest to "A". The die is the number of VPs for winning that category. Add up die value VPs. Highest VPs is winner. Tie breaker for VPs is most gold.

RATING: 7
More plays might elevate my rating of this game, because my first play was not under ideal conditions. I liked that the game is easy to teach, quick to learn, and fast to play all at the same time. The challenge of grabbing enough color cards in the early rounds, and enough gold to have strength in the auctions is very interesting. The problem I foresee in this game is the fact that memory may play a stronger role than I'd like. The player who can more accurately track who has taken what colors and how much they are worth is definitely in the power position. I wonder how the game might work if there was more open information. My first thought was to only keep hidden the cards you take for yourself in the early rounds. Don't worry, I'm not changing (ruining) the game with my own variants yet, I need to play more by the written rules, but after my first experience these were my initial thoughts. Definitely a game with strong potential to move up in rating when I've played more.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
2 phase card based game. In the first phase, each player takes it in turn to pick 4 cards, 1 at a time. Of these 4, you can save one card for yourself, put one in a face down auction pile and place 2 face up for your opponents to take. 

You can bid for the auction cards later on, which is the second phase of the game. 

The simple aim is to have the highest numeric value of a particular set of cards. There are 5 sets. There are also cards used as 1-3 gold. 

There are 2 clever mechanics in the game. In the bidding portion, you bid for cards with your gold and for gold cards with numbers of "suit" cards you are prepared to give up. The second clever  bit is the bishop cards which can be used to raise or lower the score awarded to the player with the nighest number on the cards of each set. This starts at 3 and can range from 1 to 6, as scoring is denoted with 5d6. 

This is a pretty clever mechanism for a card game and only takes 20 minutes or so to explain, set up and play to a finish. One of those fun filler type games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In the center are five dice representing different colors. The number value of the die represents the point value of that category at the end of the game. 

This game takes place in two phases. In the first, players take turns drawing cards one at a time and designating where they go: one into their hand, one into the auction pile and others equal to the # of remaining players into the public space for the other players to take. This continues around the players until the draw pile is empty.

In phase two, the top card of the auction pile is revealed and players bid on it with the cards in their hand. In the end, the player with the most value of the particular category get the points.

RATING: 7
This is a fine, "low investment, good yield" game. It is a rewarding filler in that respect and I think it deserves to be considered alongside Battle Line as one of the better of that category. Seeding the auction deck allows for long term strategy, choosing cards and bidding allows for tactical play. The decisions are interesting without being brain-burning; nor does the game overstay its welcome. The theme is original and the production is well done. Like most filler games, the theme doesn't permeate the game but I can't think of many examples where that is the case. I'm glad I own it and would definitely recommend it as one the better fillers available.

RATING: 4
Collect sets - in 2 phases, first you draft and build the auction deck, then auction off the cards put in the auction deck in phase 2.

As an abstract this is ok - but the theme and colours actually get in the way for me - I struggled a bit in low light identifying which were which in some suits :(

Theme is so paper thin (is that ironic?), and my overall feeling was the experience was pretty dull - I certainly didn't feel engaged enough to care about the outcome, not a good sign.

Quite like the draft the deck mechanic, but the lack of information you have means it isn't actually that useful, and the luck of the draw means sometimes you can't bury cards you don't want others to have. Knowing what is in the auction pile helps, but of course you won't know most of it - and that lack of info means it's impossible to know when you need to bid high for a card ... 

For me that overwhelms any careful play you can make - and the sleeping cards guarantee you can't card count/deduce what others have. So first part of the game (draft) is ok, second part (auction) I didn't like at all.

Overall - a game I'd play if nothing else was on offer, certainly not interested in owing it and many other games I'd rather play. For a drafting filler Fairy Tale beats this hands down and it's only the drafting bit that interests me!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game is just a joy to play.  It's one of those rare games that you can teach in a minute or two yet it is full of tough choices that keep you coming back for more.  The first phase, the gift phase, can often have a bit of a push your luck element.  Do you keep a decent card or send it to the gift pile or auction pile in hopes of drawing something even better?  And the agony when you are faced with having to gift a card on your final draw and it ends up being a great card (why do I never draw single gold coin cards in this situation?!!)

The second phase, the auction phase, is equally as enjoyable.  Even with two players, which is how I always play, the auction phase holds interest.  This usually isn't true for two players, but in this game it just works.

I also love how you eliminate 21 cards from the deck at the beginning of a 2p game.  This gives the whole game an air of uncertainty right up to the end as you don't know what is and isn't in play.

Almost all games are agonizingly close and this, coupled with the short play time, ensure the game gets played over and over.  Me and my wife have no problem playing a full night of this game.  It's just that fun.  Go ahead...do it..add it to your cart and checkout.  You won't be disappointed (just be prepared to air it out for a day or two..everything you hear about the funky smell is true).

Edited 11-17-2011:  Has lost some of its luster after many plays.  Still a solid game that I enjoy very much.  Dropped to an 8.

RATING: 7.2
Juego de cartas curioso. En una primera fase del juego, cada jugador se queda con una carta para sí, otra para la segunda fase, y otras tres, que van escogiendo por turno el resto.
Cuando se acaba el mazo, comienza la segunda fase, en la que se van descubriendo las cartas que fueron apartadas. Si es un libro, se puja por ello en dinero. Si es dinero, se puja con cartas.

Además, hay cartas que permiten variar el valor de los dados, que a su vez, son los que dan valor a cada color de cartas. Sencillo, elegante, rápido.. sin grandes pretensiones.

[b]TOTAL = 383.5/50 = 7.67[/b]


:thumbsup: [b]POSITIVE POINTS:[/b]

++ A great filler that is played in two phases: First a draw and split cards among yourself, the pool and the auction (where you have an incomplete knowledge of the cards since you do this, one card at a time) and then, for the second half of the game, the auction/bidding phase, you try to buy the cards to get the majorities you are aiming for.
++ Small table footprint and portable game that can be played really almost anywhere.
++ Great game insert which hold everything in an orderly fashion (though the box is a bit too big for nothing)
++ Super easy to teach, super fast to set-up and fast to play.
 

:thumbsdown: [b]NEGATIVE POINTS:[/b]

-- The small memory aspect of the game, sometimes annoys my wife, as she see that I have an advantage over her.
-- The box is a bit too big for nothing (though the book look of it is great!)
-- I'm not a theme fanatic, but the theme is just pasted on, as it could have been anything and it would work (it is more an abstract, so instead of calling thing the right name, according to the theme, say like "Pigments" card, we just say things like "Value 3 blue" card).
-- At the 2-player count, the game is more predicable, and offer less replayability (better at 3+ player count).
-- Lightweight.

:arrowE: [b]OTHER GAME INFO:[/b]
[b]
Game Weight = 1.7/5
Release Date = 2007
Number of Player = 2-4
2-player length = 15 min.
Player Count Preference = Best at 3, great at 2 and 4! :thumbsup::thumbsdown:
[/b]

RATING: 5
Updated 8/17/10.

After hearing rave reviews about Scripts & Scribes from Geekbuddies who had managed to snag a first edition from Dr. Finn, I had an Artscow version prepared.  The quality of the Artscow cards probably detracts a little from my enjoyment, and I would love to get my hands on an copy of the original.   

Basically, Scripts & Scribes combines a semi-blind card draft, an auction, and a very feeble stock manipulation mechanic to produce one of the better set majority/plurality games I've encountered. Mechanically, it's an interesting game, but I struggle to connect with it because it lacks any sort of thematic explanation for the action.  We're auctioning off items to try to collect the most of a few types of items (ideally, the ones that end up being the most valuable).  But there's no story arc, no cohesion.  We could easily have played a similar game with a Sticheln deck.  And that is precisely where my disappointment lies.  It's a game that's hard to invest in emotionally, and as a result the outcome often feels meaningless.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Biblios is a very clever card game and much more enjoyable than a first read of the rules led me to believe. It is a card game consisting of five different suits, money cards, and some "point tweaker" cards.

The game is in two halves, somewhat like For Sale. The first half players take turns dishing out cards (one for me, one for you, one for the auction pile...) and there's a pleasant angst in where you have to decide how much you value the card in front of you over what else might crop up.

The 2nd half players auction off the cards that were dished out to the auction pile, bidding money for suit cards and bidding suit cards for money.

It's a slick game that plays fast with plenty of player interaction. I dig it and wouldn't mind owning a copy at some point.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A delightful filler that lived up to expectations. Tense decisions in the first round of where to place cards (hand, auction, public offer) since you can only look at 1 card at a time, but also keeps everyone involved since they will get a card too. Then the auctions start where everyone bids on the cards from the auction pile using either gold or cards from their hand. While this is going on players can also influence the value of each set at the end of the game based on certain clergy cards. A quick 30 minute game that offers some good decisions. Since you also discard some cards randomly at the start of each game you're never sure what cards may be out of the game. I only wish the theme was a bit better for non-gamers to be interested in.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 3
A basic area influence game of sorts with an auction phase at the end and some hidden information. The turn structure is as follows: draw cards from the deck which has 5 influence sets, a money set, and a mess with the value of the area majority fights set. Keep 1 card, leave X out where X is the number of other players so they can each draft 1, and toss a single card into the future auction pile. Build up a hand. Once the deck is exhausted, auction the cards that are in that deck using the money set cards to build up bigger hand majorities and/or to mess with the value of the influence fights again. VPs based on who wins the aforementioned influence fights wins.

This isn't a bad game in the abstract, but I honestly can't imagine getting excited about such a run of the mill overall package. Reminds me of King of Siam in that way, I guess if I was dying for a filler that has these sorts of elements I would find it decently engaging, but I'm not and so I don't. Knowing what is in the auction pile can be very important, and is more than touch unpredictable as well, as there are enough cards in that to swing majorities in a major way at the end of the game, but knowing when you should spend deep or when you should sit pat is a partial crapshoot. Not impressed.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Cheap game, quick to learn, small easy to take with you to game nights. This is a filler game with a bit more strategy and time needed to play. It's a press your luck style game with multiple phases that keep it interesting. It can stand on it's own, just barely, but usually played as a filler. We always have a good time playing and teaching this game to others. Plays well with 2 players, but more fun with more. This game is out of print, so grab it if you see it.

RATING: 8.5
Simple game that scales well from 2-4. Each player tries to get the highest value in five categories. Inevitably, a player cannot get the highest in every category and must focus on what they can. The first half of the game is the "gift" (or allocation) phase where one gets cards "for free" and the second half is where players auction off the remaining cards. It works very well and plays quickly.

RATING: 10
My favorite 3 player card game.  Some great looking dice that are only used to show their current values.  Quick, fun play with interesting decisions.  "What to keep and what to put in the auction pile for later?  Did I control what cards I gave away that turn??  First part is a card draft and the second part an auction for the first round's auction pile.

RATING: 4
Biblios made it to my Spiel 2010 list, but unfortunately due to printing problems the game couldn’t make it in time for the fair. Fast forward a few months and I was able to play the game at a fair. It turned out to be a quick cardgame where the players first divide up a large deck of cards by allocating, one at a time, one card to themselves, one to an auction deck, and one card to every other player. A player draws all these cards in succession, but must decide upon the allocation immediately after seeing the card. After every card is allocated the remainder is auctioned with the purpose of building up several majorities of various resources, while at the same time sparingly altering their value. That value determines the VPs, and most VPs win.

The game plays pleasantly quickly enough, and the material in the Iello edition is gorgeous. But the game was a bit... I dunno. Out of control, perhaps? There is a good deal of guessing what to do with cards, and then there is the fact that with low player numbers, a significant amount is withdrawn from the deck at random. It creates a bit of turn angst, without doubt, but it’s not turn angst of a kind I find enjoyable. I’m not a card games player, but if I compare to Jaipur, then [i]that[/i] game allows for much more direct control over what you do and don’t. As a result, although Biblios is not really a bad game, I just couldn’t bring myself to play a second game.

RATING: 7.5
Setting aside the thin veneer of a theme, this is a game about collecting the best cards you can in various categories, and at times trying to manipulate their relative value for scoring points at the end.  What makes the game unique is the two phases.  

First you select cards and assign them to yourself, the "grab bag" for other players, or to an auction pile.  The auction pile is then sold off one by one, and players are using previously collected cards to bid on them.  The challenge is to manage your inventory to get better cards, not knowing what's coming up next.

Simple, light - works fine with 2 players.  But I'm really curious to try this with more.

RATING: 7
Scripts and Scribes
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Great card filler game which is easy to grasp and has a good amount of strategy/luck for both players and non-players. 
There are two different parts in this game. First part is drafting, second auctioning the leftover cards. Both parts are interesting and fun. You will almost never know how much points you really need for each color so you don't know who will really win in most games.
Sadly my only experience with this game is two player game, but I believe this could change soon - and if it would be good, I can see the increase a rating for a bit.

What I like:
- simple rules, you can teach the game in a minute before first play
- for this is just a card game, there are a lot of mechanisms included (set collection, hand management, auction/bidding, card drafting). Each are nice implemented and easy remembered.
- game flow is superfast. The game time (two player games) is between 10-15 minutes. Setup and tear down is also super quick.
- great game box looking as a book

What I dislike:
(there is nothing I dislike about this game, but I will try to sum of potential negative things)
- the luck in card draw could be too high for somebody (I don't care personally but I can see it could be an issue)
- the art on the cards is too repetitive and I would say mediocre
- this is very light filler game good for game openings, don't expect anything else

RATING: 7
The theme is odd, but this is actually a stockmarket game where you try to gather the more shares in 5 family and try to ensure that those family will score a much VP as possible.

+ For a self edited game, the rules are surprisingly clear and the components are of good qualities.
+ Many choices and decision taking in a short playing time 20-30 min.

- Some players doesn't like the winner take it all effect. Personaly I think it's appropriate for this kind of game and keeps tension until the end of the game, moreover the game doesn't pretend to be a strategy game where you control everything. Anyway like in most card games there's some luck so you can play several games and add the scores to mitigate this.
- The artwork could be better.

A good surprise, a very fine and subttle card game wich definitly deserve a larger audience.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Others find this concept more original than I do. You select about half your hand by choosing from among the cards you draw. Then, you acquire the balance of your hand by bidding on all the cards, one at a time, that no players selected in the first phase. You use some of the cards you selected in the first phase to make bids in the second phase, discarding those cards if you win the bid. You try to find the right balance in your hand between cards used for bidding and cards that will help you gain majorities. 
Other games have used a similar 'choose your card' method to select hands, and, of course, auctioning cards is common; putting the two together in this way is a neat trick, but I'm not sure the game justifies the hype. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.7
[September 2017 - 7.7]
A lot of people compare Biblios to For Sale (my favorite filler game), so I definitely wanted to check it out. While I enjoy Biblios, I still think For Sale, and even No Thanks, are better. The latter two create a little more emotion in the bidding, whilst there is more hidden information in Biblios that you're not really sure where others stand and what cards will come up in the auction. I really like the die (point) manipulation aspect of the game (kinda like a stock market), but sometimes I feel as if there are not enough of those cards that show up, and you're left with mostly 3-point dice, just as you started the game.

These are picky complaints, though and the game is still a lot of fun, fast and easy to explain.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Players are monks, acquiring books.  Solid two player super filler, split into two phases.  The first phase, the players take turns to draft four cards, one at a time, into their hand, and auction pile, and to the gift pile.  The other players then each take one of the gift cards.  This is repeated until the deck is empty.  Then the auction pile is auctioned off, one card at a time, and a winner is determined.  Cards drafted during the first phase of the game are used to bid in the second phase of the game - very much in the style of For Sale.  The object of the game is to hold card majorities in five suits, to get the scoring die in that suit (which can be valued between 1 and 6, depending on game events).  Highest die total acquired wins.  Feels like I've played it before in other guises (For Sale, several Knizia's), but rock solid and fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I enjoy playing this but getting other people interested in playing it is a little tougher.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The rules are much simpler than it seems when you read them, but the gameplay is deeper and more subtle than it seems when you first play it.  It has the simplicity of a game like Lost Cities, but the card evaluations and decision making are more interesting.  I've tried it with 2 and 3 players so far, it's addictive and I've been enjoying it a lot lately.

Update: With 4 players the game becomes a bit more random, it's hard to tell whether you are winning a category or not.  This isn't a bad thing, just a noticeable difference from the 2 player game.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An easy pick, when I'm looking for a lighter game that won't be over too quickly. Despite it's lighter elements, still an intriguing experience. 

The first phase is a mechanic I haven't seen anywhere else: you must give a card to both partners, yourself and the future auction pile, but you only draw one at a time. You think "This is a great card, but could I draw something better for myself?" or "It's only a little money, but the next card has to go to me - what's if it's worse?" The second phase may just be pretty straight-forward auctioning, but the genius is in the lead-up to it through phase one.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Biblios has recently been republished. I missed it first time around and am very glad to have found it now. It is a card game with two phases. You spend the first part of the game distributing the cards to each player and to an auction stack. Then the second part of the game is spent auctioning off the auction stack. Cards are either Gold (which you pay for in other cards) or one of the five sets (which you pay for in gold). 

Throw in a clever points mechanism which determines the value of each set to the person with the majority at the end of the game, and you have an excellent 45 minute game.

RATING: 4
Visually beautiful game, but lacking in interesting strategy decisions.  Theme pasted-on and does not engage the player.  Play consists of a "gift phase" in which players must decide whether to keep, auction or give away cards.  This phase is mildly interesting as decisions must be made as cards are drawn one by one.  Then play shifts into the "Auction phase," in which cards are auctioned.  Memory of what one has put in the pile becomes important here.  In all, game play strikes me as bland and flavorless; when I asked my wife if she wanted to play again, she immediately named a half dozen games she would prefer, and I agreed with her.

Minor annoyances: cards are extremely stiff and difficult to shuffle, and the storage well for them is badly designed -- it allows you to remove about 2/3 of the cards with ease, but you can't get the others without inverting the box.

I have yet to introduce the game, without players wanting a second try, and given its short playtime, its easy to oblige.

RATING: 7
This game is great and has a lot of my gaming prereqs: short time, auction elements, card-based, randomization through card removal, and a simple ruleset. A surprising amount of game and tension is built into a 25 minute experience. 

One minor flaw I've seen in the game is that the 3rd and 4th players are at fairly large disadvantages. I'd say that the 2nd player is probably the strongest at the start of the game. He/she has first choice of the first draft, and immediately after has an opportunity to pick from the deck. Maybe give 1 gold to player 3 and 2 gold to player 4? After a couple more plays: yep, the 4th player is definitely, definitely at a disadvantage. By the time it's your turn, a lot of secret information and choice cards have been obtained by your opponents. The hole you start in is significant.

At 50 plays I am convinced that the 4th player disadvantage is factual.

RATING: 8.5
The drafting of Fairy Tale meets the auctions of For Sale.  Fantastic super filler, that I'm long not sick of after multiple plays.  Features a draft phase and an auction phase, as players try to build up their hand to get point-scoring majorities in the five different categories (suits), which will earn victory points (represented by dice, the value of which can also be manipulated).  The heart of the game revolves around the hidden information of what categories other players are going for, and the surprise at the end when cards are revealed is tense and exciting.  Equally good with 2, 3 or 4.  Also features one of the best box covers ever! (designed to look like a book)  Outstanding game in its class!  Only negative is the cardstock quality - the cards don't shuffle well and damage easily.  Magnificent artwork though!  

See [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/636072]my pictorial review[/url].

For strategy see my article: [thread=633521][/thread]
See also: [thread=634627][/thread]

Custom [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/40596/item/2120752#item2120752]stamp collecting rethemed[/url] deck is great!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
S&S is one of my favorite games. I rate it a 10, as relative to its genre, I'd rather play this. Yes, it's light but the strategy is surprisingly deep.  It's a game similar to For Sale in that there are two phases. You collect cards in each phase but the first acquisition phase merely sets you up for the auction where most of the fun happens. 

In the auction, you pay for suit cards with gold but pay for gold cards with (any) cards played face down so people don't know what you're discarding. You can openly collect a majority of cards in a suit but then shave them down secretly knowing that everyone else has abandoned that category as "lost" to you.  I've shaved cards down in the auction phase from 6 points to 1 (and won) because everyone knew I had a lot of cards and stopped competing with me. [i]I thought you had a lot of that?! Well, I DID...[/i] You need to bid gold cards for gold cards just to keep others from getting cheap gold and to make them think you have more gold than you really do.

There's a lot of psychological play in convincing others to back off because you have something wrapped up and to being sneaky about pursuing a category. Trying to predict who is collecting which suits is not always obvious and you have to mess with other players in the auction to the point of sometimes getting stuck with stuff that you were just trying to bid up.

RATING: 7
Biblios has such a simple mechanic but man it can leave with you a lot of tough decisions; is this the best card I will draw?  Do I take it?  Do I put it in the auction pile?  Do I put it in the public space?  Effectively you know ALMOST every pertinent detail in the game, minus the removed cards, but the draw will curve your optimal strategy but even if that doesn't pan out, you can manipulate the end scoring.  So simple but so clever!

I am not usually one for auction games but this has almost more of a betting feel to it, but you better not get caught without the gold to back up your lies!

Biblios hits a similar spot as Sea of Clouds with a greater degree of control; while it may not be as exciting it is definitely more strategic with less take that.

With all that said this is quite a relaxing game to play, it's not a brain-burner, there's very little conflict but it will definitely not lull you into complacency or boredom.

RATING: 4
Summary: Clever numbered card game with auction and stock-market like elements.

Rating history:
1st play: :star::star::star::nostar::nostar:

4p - Fairly busy and all-or-nothing with 4p. Probably better with less.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
2011
My friend Joel Lytle in New York called my attention to Scripts & Scribes, a couple of years ago, and I have been trying to purchase this card game ever since.  I learned Steve Finn was republishing it under the title Biblios, and immediately placed a pre-order last fall, which arrived this afternoon.  

Gaming friends came over and with a few minutes read on the rules we were playing.  There are two phases.  Cards are "gifted" then an auction phase follows and a portion  of the "gifted" cards are auctioned.  There are five categories and the highest card score in each gains the victory points for that category registered on a die that players can adjust throughout the game with Church cards.  Interesting, in the auction, Gold Cards are used to purchase category cards, whereas unknown, face down cards are used to purchase Gold Cards.  I lot of juggling goes on.

The description here does not do the game justice.  You best try to calculate who is saving and doing what.  Strategy is convoluted.  The is a lot of uncertainty in the game, and when you think you are setting yourself up for a high score, you may indeed be setting up your opponent. Technically, the maximum number of victory points in the game is 19, but with 3 players, 7 victory points won the game each time.  

I don't think the box has much shelf appeal, but the contents are attractive and good quality.  This card game fits nicely into a compact box with a magnetic closure.  Play is 20 mins with 3 people.  

I am sure we will be playing this game again and again and again.

RATING: 7
A simple to learn and clever card game.  Great for Gamers and a good vehicle to introduce non-gamers to a more diverse game world.  Played with non-gamers and parents who only knew card games like Hearts, Spades, Poker and UNO.  It was a little tough at first breaking up their card game paradigm, but soon they were right in the swing of it.  Themeatic card art, and good quality cards.  The only negative is the card lay out.  The art dominates the card and the text on the card (naming the type of card) is small font and is hard to read as it is layered on the art. It makes the cards confusing for new players and hard to read in general.

RATING: 8
An amazing filler game.  It feels a little like For Sale in that there are two halves to the game and it centers around a bidding mechanic.  In the first half you take turns dividing cards among players and an auction pool trying to create the best hand to have bidding power in the second.  In the second half you use your hand to acquire more cards in order to gain majorities in one of five categories.  There are some agonizing decisions to be made, and it plays very fast.

RATING: 8
First off. let me say I got this game from the designer in a "free just pay shipping" try it promotion. I asked for it because it sounded interesting. This game is VERY good! We have only played it 2 player so far but it was a lot of fun. the mechanics are solid and the game seems well balanced as games always seem to come out close. The choices during the donation phase can be almost AP causing in a fun way. The "one card at a time" draw is what does it. Keep it? auction it? give it away? Arrgg..

The quality is very good for a self-publish. I really like the card quality. There are a few of the cards that are cut off center causing a white edge on some of the backs but it's not too big a problem and I would imagine would be addressed in a bigger print run. Which I hope this game gets. It is worth it. 

The game plays in a relatively small space. My wife and I played it a few times on a 2 person cafe table while our kids were in a pottery class and there was room to spare.

RATING: 6
Players draft cards for points in order to win each of five objectives or that they can use as currency in an auction of the cards rejected during the draft. Once all cards have been drafted and auctioned, players compare their total points in each of the five objectives. Each objective will be worth some VP which can be influenced during the draft and auction by certain cards. The winner is the player with the most VPs.

Lite filler game, some luck in the draft, bluffing. Good components with Ok art.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
It's a good game, I just don't see why anyone would play it over For Sale. They're both quick fillers with 2 phases where the second phase is an auction where your resources are defined in the first phase, except that I much prefer the first phase of For Sale and For Sale is faster.My issues with the first phase of Biblios is firstly regarding randomness. I like push your luck as a mechanism, but there's not much to it here: either you hope to get a better card or settle. There's no pacing arch or interesting probabilities or extra reward for pushing your luck further. My second issue is the church cards. Depending on the player count and when they show up they will be either very important or completely useless, and while that is an interesting arch, that doesn't change the fact that they're so boring to get sometimes, especially the first turn. My final issue is the biggest one, and that is that the decisions in this game are almost all completely obvious. If you draw a 1 gold, you're going to put it in the middle. If you're in the middle of the game and you see a good card for a colour you haven't focused on, you shouldn't bother. If you have a choice between a 3, 2 or 1 gold from the middle, you're going to take the 3. Maybe the game is just worse at 4 players because of the amount of gold cards in the deck, but they are just so static and uninteresting. Also, the competition for majorities is so fierce at 4 players that you have to pick 1 or 2 colours and really go for it in order to be competitive, which leaves out a lot of interesting decisionmaking. It would have been a lot more interesting if there was a way to trade cards with each other, to incentivise picking that 4 brown even though you don't have any other browns.The second phase of the game, I really like. I like that you can throw away your worst colours to win a gold card that may help you get that final edge for a colour you really care about. It's interesting to try to inflate the price of a card you don't want and how you can try to force your opponent to exhaust their money to get a lead in a colour you know there are better cards for coming up later. It's just that first phase that I feel drags on and is uninteresting, but it's so vital for the second phase that the game in its entirety just isn't as fun for me as it could have been.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Biblios (3rd English edition) is easy to learn, fast to play, and reasonably fun with 2 players. I admire the genius of the game designer. He created a game that seems completely different from the other games I've played, but after just one game I felt like I could play it competently. 

My husband and I both tend toward analysis paralysis and poor memory. These problems were not an issue in this smoothly flowing game, where decisions are limited in each turn and a quick glance at your hand and the board is all you need when making a decision. 

I would like to try this game with more players because the mechanisms of the gift and auction phases would probably be much more exciting than they are with 2.

This game is beautifully produced, with evocative artwork, solid components, and a lovely box to hold everything. My only complaint is that the cards are just a little too stiff and shiny. This game is one of the few in my collection that I consider to be a candidate for card sleeves. I will probably play it often enough to make sleeving the cards worthwhile.

I ordered the game directly from the designer. He shipped the game within hours of my order and provided timely email updates about the process. Even if your FLGS or OLGS carries the game, I recommend the direct-order route for outstanding service.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Biblios is a good game to play with casual gamers.  This game is easy to understand, with some luck because you draw cards from a deck.

The goal of the game is to have the most point at the end of the game.  For each of the 5 colors, the player with the highest total on his cards will win the dice corresponding to that color.  Dices are not roll, it only indicate the number of points each color worth.  Some card allow players to increase or decrease value of a particular color.
On your turn you draw a number of cards (number of player + 1) one by one and for each of them you have to decide what to do with it.  You must keep one card for yourself, put a card away for the auction phase later and put the rest of the card face up on the table.  These card will be taken by your opponnent (they choose a card in clockwise order).
After the deck of cards is exhausted you shuffle the cards that were put away for the auction phase.
Each of these cards are put to auction one by one.  If the card is one of the 5 color or a priest card (special card to change value of a dice) they are bought with gold card.  If the card is a gold (value from 1 to 3) players bid with a number of cards they want to discard instead of paying with gold.

When auction deck is exhausted the game is over.  For each of the 5 color, you check who has more points in that particular color and takes the die of that color.  Each player add the total of his dice and the player with the highest total wins the game.

RATING: 7
Well I was suppose to write a review for this one, but it was denied for being to short.  I personally think there are way too many 'long reviews' around here and not enough short concise reviews.  (most rules do not need to be rehashed).

So here goes, my comment/review:

I'm becoming a big fan of independently produced games.  This is no disappointment.  The cards, box, etc. are of good quality.  The rules are well written (although they may be on to small side print wise).  The box is a perfect size for the components. Is this really all that?  

It's a really interesting auction game.  I very much enjoy the two very distinct phases to this game.  The first phase, is really a 'drafting' of the hands (pot).  In this phase you get an interesting choice of what you want versus what you are willing to give your opponents, versus what you think you might want to bid for in the second phase of the game. 

The second phase is building your scoring hand for the end.  The cards in your hand can be used to 'bid' on cards or just saved for end game scoring.  Gold cards are used to buy paintings and Bishops.  And any combination of cards can be used to 'buy' gold cards.  Gold cards are only used in tie breakers at the end, so they are often better to use then save.  But, again, you don't know if something better is going to com up later.

End scoring is simple.  Who ever has built the best collection in each of the 5 categories scores the value of that 'collection'.  The only problem is those values will change based on the selection of the bishops.  All collections start at a value of 3.  When Bishops come into play either in the 1st or 2nd phase.  The bump up or down the value of 1 or 2 collections.

That's the game.  Fun, quick game.  

smell: -------:what:-------

RATING: N/A
Opinió després de una lectura de regles:
Joc ràpid (duració de filler) que combina mecàniques de "draft" i de subasta en dues fases diferenciades del joc. En una primera fase, cada jugador roba de la baralla de cartes tantes cartes com jugadors més 1 d'una en una. Una d'aquestes cartes la col·loca apart (formant el mazo de subasta), una altre la col·loca davant seu (per robarla a la mà) i les restants les col·loca al mig de la taula (per que les agafin la resta de jugadors en ordre). Es segueix fins que s'acabin totes les cartes i, posteriorment, es pasa a subastar d'una en una les cartes del mazo de subasta. 
Sembla que l'atzar en el ordre en el que es roben les cartes pot ser molt determinant, no m'acaba de convencer que, un cop has escollit quina carta et quedes, la resta les agafen la resta de jugadors sense que puguis fer res (pot pasar que et quedis una carta més o menys bona, enviis un altre al mazo de subastes i les restants que treguis siguin molt millors, de manera que surten beneficiats els altres jugadors).
Tot i que no té res a veure, m'ha recordat (en profunditat i en tipus de joc) al Speicherstadt i, en el mecanisme de draft, al 7 Wonders.

RATING: 2.5
Played it once, and don't have a strong desire to play it again.  The total points that there can be in the game range from 5 to 30 (5 categories, each with a score of 1 to 6).  That seems like a really low number to divide among 4 players, and leads to the score being very tight.  That is, small perturbations can cause huge differences in final ranking.  That's bad, because a player with a great memory can keep track of all the cards that have been drafted, which leads to a disproportionally huge advantage.

It may seem like a fun game to new gamers who are used to this kind of low-quality fare, but memory games don't interest me that much when there are so many great games to play instead.

RATING: 7.7
045 minutes
2-phase game of collectors trying to get the most valuable art pieces.
In turn, until out of cards in draw deck, draw cards and deal some to your opponents, one to you, one "for later auction". Influence current price for each art category accordingly.
Then all go for an auction of the cards that were left aside, using the cards you took in the first phase to pay (hopefully not too much!) to win each auction - or try to make a "friend" pay more...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
(10/2012) Deceptively simple rules, yet profound play that finishes within 20-30 minutes. How is it that a card game with relatively sparse components be so much fun to play? The card selection mechanic is similar to Merchants of Amsterdam, where the active player will draw cards, one at a time, deciding if they are going to keep it, put it up for auction, or put it in a pile where it will be given away, without looking at the next card. The choices are deliciously agonizing, and some memorization is needed to remember what cards were placed in the auction pile. The cards are one of five suits, in two or three distinct ranks, or money of one of three denominations, or church cards that can alter the relative value of one of the five suits. After all player have selected their cards, either by secretly or openly drafting them, the auction cards are auctioned off one at a time. If it is a suit card, then money is bid. If it is a money card, then number of suit cards are bid. In the center, there are five dies representing the relative value of each suit. As mentioned before, the church cards can increase or decrease the value by altering the die. In the end, whomever has the highest total in card rank in each suit will win the respective die value. It is possible for a player to win several dies. Highest total value of the dies determines the winner.

The theme is thin, as in our first games we did not recognize nor care what the suits represented. In that matter, the theme could be anything. Rules and components were reasonably good. All in all, this is a fun, compact game that doesn't feel like a filler. Initial rating is an '8', with room to move up.

Update (02/02/13) 5 plays: Liked it so much, I got my own copy. Cards are very stiff and shiny--nice at first, but very easy to smudge with finger oils, and the edges chip after one play! Strongly recommend sleeving this one, and soon!

Update (11/16/13) 11 plays: Played two 2-player games, each at under 15 minutes--the gift phase taking 5 minutes, and the auction phase taking 10 minutes. Not bad for a quick 2-player filler!

Update (04/18/2015) 25 plays: Solid, solid, solid card drafting game. Bound to be one of the future "classics". Solid "8".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
◎將遊戲圖板放在桌面中央，圖板上的空格放上對應顏色的骰子，所有骰子將「3」朝上。
◎依照人數移除對應數量的卡片
▲2人遊戲－移除6張金幣卡(每種面額各2張)和21張隨機的卡片。
▲3人遊戲－移除3張金幣卡(每種面額各1張)和12張隨機的卡片。
▲4人遊戲－移除7張隨機卡片。
◎移除卡片後將剩餘的卡片洗牌，面向下形成抽牌堆。
1.禮物階段
◎隨機選擇一位起始玩家，順時針進行。
◎輪到玩家的回合時，先從抽牌堆抽牌
▲2人遊戲－抽3張
▲3人遊戲－抽4張
▲4人遊戲－抽5張
◎玩家抽牌後先看過牌，接著將牌分配到以下的區域
▲1張面向下放在自己面前
▲1張面向下放在拍賣牌堆上
▲其餘的牌面向上放在公共區域
◎抽牌時一次抽一張，分配完後再抽第二張，依此類推，直到抽完指定的張數。
◎分配結束後玩家將置於面前的牌加入手牌，其餘的人順時針依序選擇1張公共區域的牌加入手牌。
◎待所有人都增加一張手牌後，玩家回合結束，輪到左手邊的玩家抽牌分配，持續進行到抽牌堆被抽完為止。
2.拍賣階段
◎將拍賣牌堆洗牌形成新的抽牌堆。
◎由禮物階段的起始玩家開始，翻開拍賣牌堆最上方的那張牌，面向上置於桌面中央進行拍賣。
◎起始玩家翻牌前將抽牌堆置於自己面前，以免忘記輪到誰的回合。
◎如果翻開的牌是金幣，玩家以五大指標卡的張數為貨幣出價競標，數字的顏色不限可混合使用，得標者將應付的牌面向下置入棄牌堆，不要給其他玩家看到。
◎如果翻開的牌不是金幣，玩家以金幣競標牌，得標者將應付的金幣出示給所有玩家看到後，置入棄牌堆。如果支付的金幣大於標價，不找零。
◎由翻開牌的玩家開始出價，出價可以出1或更多，也可以選擇pass。
◎接著輪到左手邊的玩家出價，順時針進行。
◎出價時要比前一位玩家的價高，如果pass，則不能再參與此回合的拍賣。
◎出價直到價高者得標後，再進行下一回合的競標。
◎如果每位玩家都選擇pass，則將牌置入棄牌堆。
◎如果最高價者付不出對應的牌將受到處罰，所有其他玩家可以從該玩家的手牌抽走一張佔為己有，原本拍賣的牌重新拍賣，被處罰的玩家不能參與競標。
◎除罰變體：被處罰的人必須由他左手邊的玩家隨機抽一張手牌置入棄牌堆，並不得參與重新競標。

教會卡
◎在遊戲中任何時候(無論是禮物階段選手牌選到或是競標階段得到)玩家得到教會卡，遊戲暫停，立刻執行教會卡的效果，或選擇不執行直接棄牌。
◎教會卡可以改變各類別骰子的點數，左上角的數字代表增減的點數，右上角代表可以調整幾顆骰子(如果是2顆必需是不同顏色的骰子)。
◎如果是+1/-1，則玩家可以自行選擇要+1或是-1。
◎教會卡執行效果後置入棄牌堆。

遊戲結束
◎當所有的牌都被買走或置入棄牌堆，遊戲結束開始記分。
◎玩家計算自己的手牌在各顏色的分數，每一個顏色分數最高的玩家，可以拿走該顏色的骰子，置於自己面前(維持骰子的點數不變)。
◎如果玩家的手牌分數平手，則比較手牌右下角的英文字母，最接近A的玩家贏得該顏色的骰子。
◎將贏得的骰子點數相加，點數最多的玩家獲勝；如果平手，則手牌有最多黃金的玩家獲勝；若平手，比較手牌僧侶(咖啡色)的分數(平手比字母)；若還是平手，則依照圖板從左到右的順序，接著比顏料(藍色)的分數，直到分出勝負為止。

RATING: 6
First played June 23rd, 2008. Taught in 10min, played in 20min with two players. This is an interesting push your luck game. Balance seems to be weighted in luck, however there is some strategy in it. The board consists of 5 categories of which 2 are workers(values 2-4; 2 of 4's, 3 3's, 4 2's) and 3 are resources(values 1-2; 7 1's, and 2 2's) each start with a die value of 3 and can go 1 to 6. Deck is comprised of: 9 of each of the 5 category cards and 9 of the bishop cards (lets you change the value plus/minus when owned) which have different values on them. There are also 33 gold cards with values of 1,2,3(11 of each). In a two player game, remove 2 of each gold value card. Shuffle the remaining cards and randomally remove 21 cards. For the first phase of the game, each player on their turn takes three cards and evaluates them one at a time. You have three options. Give the card to your opponent, place it in the bidding pile, and keep the card for yourself. Do each of these actions once each. If you take a bishop card, immediatly do the adjustment of the value plus or minus of one of the categories. If you get a plus/minus two, you must change two categories. Rotate clockwise around until all cards have been drawn. The second phase you bid on cards. Shuffle the cards set aside for bidding. Each player may bid higher or pass. Once you pass, you are out of the bidding. For gold card, you bid category cards. For category card, you bid an amount of gold(no change is made if you don't have exact). After the bidding is over, the player who has the combine high points of each category gets that die's value. Ties are set to the side. The winner is the player with the highest score.

RATING: 8.5

The actual game is an auction and set collection game, but pretty far removed from Ra.  You spend the first half of the game doing a fun card drafting bit that will induce moans and groans. I enjoyed it and look forward to trying it with some more players.

My wife hasn't been too taken with it.  I'm partial to the bluffing aspects at this time.

RATING: 7
Biblios is an enjoyable mix of a light card-drafting game and a light auction game. I stress "light" because much of the potential information needed to make a good decision is hidden, turning what could be a very tactical game into more of a luck-pushing affair.

Still, it provides some enjoyable moments (especially in the auction phase) and is very accessible to new players, making it a good game night warm-up game.

RATING: 8

The two-phase gameplay (drafting and then auction) works very well as you auction gold cards for point cards (and manipulators) and (any) cards for gold cards. The game only lasts one round so it is quick playing.  Works very well for two.  Three player is just as much fun, and the battle for the workers and resources is intensified.

Initial Rating : 8.5 (April 2011)

I really like this light medium card game, it plays so quickly but I´m always satisfied with it. I´m not sure why but I find myself with a longing to play Biblios. It is a deceptively simple game but it has a surprising depth, you also need to exercise you memory, it has an auction and a partial secret draft phase and it has a little of “take that” in it too. All its mechanics work very well together and it has lots of interesting decisions in the game. Good tension :D.

The game box is also pretty cool.

All in all, I recommend this game. One of the best card games out there.

Current Rating: 8.0

It has some luck in it, but in general, the best player will win. 

My only complaint is that, once I sleeved all the cards, they won´t fit into the box :(.

RATING: 8
Great game!  One of only two games I will sleeve.  The cards are a hard material that tends to chip and are hard to shuffle.  And that smell was overwhelming at first.  We had to spread them out on newspaper in the basement for a week before we could play the first time.  I love the way this plays with the the 2 phases (gift and auction) in about 25 minutes.  It is hard to tell who is winning.  Sometimes when you alter the dice thinking you are sabotaging the other players, you are really only hurting yourself.  The end is always a surprise!

Unsleeved the cards...let them chip, who cares?  As long as they all get played, it will be even wear on the cards.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Quick and simple game in two halves, the first being a slice-the-pie game in which players have to decide which cards to keep for themselves, which to give to the others and which to hold back for the second half of the game in which the held back cards are auctioned off. 

The twist is that as you draw cards one-by-one you can't view all the cards you'll draw on your turn before deciding what to do with them, i.e. you have to decide what to do with each card as you draw it. This means that if you draw a half-decent card you have to decide whether to keep it or not without knowing whether there's a better one just waiting to be drawn - you can only keep one card for yourself each turn.

RATING: 7
Biblios is a decent set collection/auction game. The mechanics of the "gift phase" (i.e., seeding the players' hands and auction area) make for a unique and welcome approach instead of the usual random card deal. Fairly smooth flow and rather low-conflict interaction. Overall a fun, light game with an original theme, albeit thinly implemented.

RATING: 9
Scripts and Scribes 2nd ed. - VHS case edition.  Glad to have this quick 'filler' card game in my collection. I like the idea of the Bishop cards that are dealt with as soon as 'acquired' as they alter the course of victory, I will deal at least two to the auction pile to purchase later.  There's a comfortable amount of control and flexibility in this game regardless of the obvious randomness in card draw.  Rating is for 2-player games.

NOTE TO SELF:  Go for acquiring the 'high' cards during the donation phase and focus on certain 'suite' cards during the auction phase, all while collecting 'gold' cards to purchase with... sounds easy enough.

RATING: 10
Book-like packaging hides a well thought out drafting game where you must choose the right card for yourself, your opponents… and a second deck of cards to be auctioned after the draft, all in hopes of getting victory points for the most of each colour. This is one game where you really need to pay attention to what other players are doing too, and it's quite intense as well as fun.

BIG PLUS: easy to learn, quick play, interactive, well designed
MINUS: (none)

ESSENTIAL to those who want a nice starter game that runs on different mechanics and is playable by all ages.

RATING: 8.7
Biblios is a great card game which mixes up a couple of my favorite mechanics, auctions and set collection.  The "gifting" phase is really unique and feels good, deciding whether to take that first card you see, or hoping something better comes up for you, but not for your opponents...  And then that whole feeling of if you should put it in auction and hope you get it later.  I really like that.  The auction is really good too.  Switching between paying gold for cards and then paying cards for gold, definite fun.  There's a lot of great things going for this one and I enjoy it extensively.

RATING: 6
The game is played in two phases, a drafting phase where a card is handed to each player and to an auction pile each turn and then an auction phase where the auction pile is handed out. You bid for cards with gold cards or cards from your hand. You are trying to get the highest value in 5 colors and the points each color is worth is adjustable with cards during the game.

There's nothing at all wrong with it, I just don't think it is a great deal of fun. There isn't a lot of joy in just handing out cards and then the auctions are not that interesting.

RATING: 9.5
Engaging, fun little card game. Bumped to 9 due to amazing art of release as Biblios (used to be Scripts & Scribes), and because the theme is so close to my heart.  Some of my favorite graphic design in a game,  awesome "book-box" and nice multi-colored dice.  However I have to ding it for some quality issues: cards chip even with gentle tile shuffle, so have to be sleeved.  Also card-well in insert only has thumb holes half way down, which makes the thumb holes useless; you have to turn the whole thing upside down to get the cards out.  Finally there is the notoriously strong smell when new that makes some people physically ill.

RATING: 7
This is a card collection game where only the majority in each suit wins. You get the number of points on the die associated with the suit. A handful of cards allow changing the numbers on the dice. During the selection round the dealer can decide to keep it, send it for auction, or put it out for the other players. Many of the cards are used as coins. The coins are used to buy cards during the auction round. There is some observation and memory element in tracking what colors other players prefer. This is a nice filler.

RATING: 8
This game is not the deepest game in the world so you can't compare it to a multi-layered work such as Caverna or Terra Mystica.  It is a filler, and the best of fillers in my opinion.  If you are looking for something with quite a bit of suspense and tactics that you can play in under 20 min, I have not played a better game.  It is definitely more tactics than strategy.  

It scales so well with 2-4 players.  I love it most with two but it is interesting that with 4 you have a completely different game at hand.  I was told that it is similar to For Sale except that this one doesn't get old after a while. I often have everyone asking if we can play it again, immediately after finishing one game.  

One of the best parts of the game is the self induced tension.  Almost like you are your own worst enemy, second guessing all your moves. "Was that the best move I could have done, should I have given that card instead of the other one?"  

Its one of those games that upon finishing, everyone wants to get their secrets off their chest. "I was hoping you would do this, but you went for that color so I pulled back."  "I was bluffing the whole time on those last three bids.  You totally went for it. That freed up the church card I needed." That kinda stuff.  


I can't give this game a 9 or 10 in comparing all board games, but in its own category/genre I definitely would.  I don't know a better 20min game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Tense, quick and fun. These are the things I would choose to describe Biblios. The game has two parts and the mix of them works great. The first part is push your luck. You draw cards one by one and put them into auction, your hand or give it to other players. Since you only look at one card at a time you constantly wonder if you can get something better or it is time to stop pushing and get something mediocre. The second part is much more intense! The auction is a simple one but every card discarded gives more and more information to everyone and there is tension until the last card of the auction since that might change who wins a suit and thus the winner of the game. Great filler game, highly recommend it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

コンポーネントも良く、所有欲が満たされるゲーム。「写本と修道士」の頃の絵の方が私ごのみだが、新版も悪くない。カードは傷みやすそうな飲んで、スリープは必須。ただし、スリープに入れると内箱に収まらないのが残念。

二つ目は、このシステムとテーマは全く関連性が薄いと思う。
三つ目は、サイコロがこの厳粛なテーマをぶち壊していると思う。もっと別な形で表現した方が良かった。
欠点はあるが、遊んで楽しく所有して損はないゲームだ。

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Biblios is a well-designed card game in which you go through the deck in two different ways, first by drawing cards and hoping you make the right decision about what to give away and what to keep, and second by auctioning off cards one at a time, setting yourself up with enough of the right colors to score points and win. The game is all about the fact that you never see the next card off the top of the deck until you have made a decision about the first one. I enjoyed this one for a while, but ultimately there were too many hidden factors for me and my group. You could almost call this a "memory game," but that would only account for the things you saw your opponents taking. I definitely appreciate the lean design and excellent components, but eventually this one had to go.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b]Biblios[/b] is auction game divided in 2 parts, with 5 different color dice that act as final points at the end of the game. Changing those dice through cards (+1 or -1) /based on what colors players have/expect to get/other players might have/ players prepare dice for the end of the game.

At the end of the game, in every of the 5 colors, person who has the most points in that color takes that color dye and who has the most points on dice is the winner.
In first part of the game players take cards for free (with some luck) and leave one card per turn for second part of the game, while in second part of the game players compete for cards left from first part using auction mechanism.

Clever, fun, relatively easy to explain, but needs at least game or two in order to fully understand whats going on.

RATING: 6
Very cleaver card game (the dice that are included are only used to keep scores) that is simple to teach and learn. The initial deal phase has some press your luck elements, but there is some (as in a little) strategy that, although could hardly guarantee a win, can certainly help your odds. During the 2nd auction phase, good use of cards and some memory as to what has already been played can be helpful in making educated guess. Usually it only take winning two categories to win, so a focused approach on one (with some bishop help) or two categories is all that may be needed. Overall a light and enjoyable game – especially for the cost.

RATING: 7
update 
Essen 10
reprint by Iello : biblios


This is a great cardgame. Don't get fooled by the fact that it uses dice. They are only needed to determine the value of the workers or resources by means of adjustments by playing the bisshop's cards.

Gameplay is pretty quick. And there is no risk for the game being slowed down by AP players.

Randomising the deck by leaving some cards out works here great and I guess it will offer plenty of replay value and second guessing.

If there is a reprint I''ll probably buy it

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Excellent filler which can be played in 15 minutes or less after the first play.  First part is a bit of card drafting in a sense as you look at one card at a time and choose if you wish to place it in the common area (which means the card will be selected by someone else), the auction pool (which comes up in phase 2 of the game), or in your own hand.  Phase two is the auction and you use gold cards to purchase nongold cards in the auction and just bid a number of cards to win the gold cards in the auction.  In order to win, you seek to win majorities in enough of the 5 different areas to earn the number of points on the die (which can fluctuate based on the bishops that can make the value go up or down by one).  Somewhat reminiscent of For Sale, it brings in a couple interesting twists that make it unique.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
I love a well-designed auction mechanic.  Biblios has it.  This short, easy-to-teach filler is wonderful.  It plays so fast, is highly interactive, and has push-your-luck written all over it.  It depends a good deal on one's ability to bluff.  Try to deplete your opponents stockpile of cash during the auction phase for cards that don't help you, so they are less able to bid on the cards you really want!

I am a little un-impressed with the markable cards, which are made of very thick and brittle card stock.  After a few very gentle shuffles the finish "chipped" off a some of the card corners.  Therefore, you should definitely sleeve this with a premium Fantasy Flight or Ultra Pro "standard card game" sleeve, as I have done.  TTFN

RATING: 7
Clever drafting mechanic where the active player can look at a card, and either put it out for others to draft or bury it to bid on it later.  After the cards are drafted, you auction off cards that were placed into the auction pile.  You are trying to get majorities in the color cards in the game and score points based on the dice corresponding to the color.  Purple cards allow you to moving victory points up and down throughout the game.  

Simple filler with good quality components and different theme.  I like this game a lot.

RATING: 6.5
The game has two phases, drafting and auction.  The two phases work together in synergy.  However, I find the drafting phase to be somewhat slow and repetitious, probably due to the fact that it is done one card at a time from a rather large draw pile.  I enjoy auction mechanics and this one is no exception.  The game as a whole is good, entertaining, and a good filler.  There is just something about it that I don't quite grasp and as I said the drafting phase feels not entirely satisfying.
A note about the components.  The Iello version looks better and is of better quality (bigger dice, better art) but is not as clear as the original. In the original it's much easier to see and keep track of which suits and cards the other players take because they are monochrome instead of multichrome.  I prefer the legibility and clarity to the aesthetic appeal.

RATING: 9
This game is probably my FAVORITE filler of all time.  I think it is brilliant.  It is a set collection game where you are fighting to collect the most of 5 color sets.  What is brilliant is that each turn you look at cards, one at a time, and get to keep one, gift one to each player, and set one aside for an auction later.  Then, each of the 5 colors have a value (represented by dice) that is constantly changing.  So you may win "red" in the end, but red may only be worth 1 point.  It is a very well balanced game that takes maybe 20 minutes.  I love to teach it.  I love to play it.  I think it's the perfect mix of skill and luck.

RATING: 8
As soon as I played this it got put in the bag of games I would always take out to games night/games event with me list.
The game is simple enough to teach to those who are not regular gamers as well as offering a little bit of strategy for those who play often.  More often than not we will play several games of this back to back.
At first it feels a little slow, but soon picks up pace as everyone 'gets' the idea of the game, typically we knock a game out with 4 players in around 1/2 hour, making it a great warm up or filler game.  
If you wanted to take this as a travel game you could easily do away with the little board and just back 4 dice and a pack of cards.
Certainly a game which will be staying in my collection.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
If I polled my whole family as to their favourite game this I am sure would come out of the combined list on top. It is the only game everyone will always settle on to play. The theme, I am sure, means absolutely nothing to any of them. They just love beating me because I am terrible at it!

You play as monks controlling the redistribution of bibliotheca materials. Inks, parchments, forbidden tomes and such like. The game is played in two stages. The first you redistribute the goods. One to each player and one to the auction pile, but you do this one at a time so you cannot look at the cards and then decide what goes where. Then surprisingly the auction pile is auctioned. The auction works very well, even with two, and brings a fantastic tension to the game. 

As always with good games, there are a few wrinkles to the game play. The value of the sets you are seeking a majority in can be altered during gameplay and this for me is where the fun is at. Just don't end up winning the one set you have spent most of the game devaluing (difficult to do I know, but I have managed it on several occasions!).

Just a great game, I don't think I have played it with anyone who hasn't enjoyed it. I like the way the distribution at the start slowly sucks people into the game with a few interesting decisions before the crunchy, nervous tension of trying to work out what you can win in the auction, and what cards you can bid to win more money to buy different cards in upcoming auctions, because you know the card you want and put on the auction pile at the start of the game must be coming up soon, and you really, really, really want it now, and if you had known how the game was going to go would never have put it up for auction in the first place.

Simply excellent. Probably one of my top 10 games. Definitely a keeper until I finally win a game then I will probably become unbearable and someone else will sell it!

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is brilliant. It feels nothing like any other card game I've ever played, and it's a blast to play. Biblios is one of my favorite card games.

The theme is original and nicely expressed through the gameplay, and the two-phase structure makes for a game that's somehow both calm -- like a monastery -- and packed with tough decisions.

Like Stone Age and Lords of Scotland, Biblios hits a strategy/tactics sweet spot for me. You can go in with a plan, and carry that plan through the game, but you'll have to change that plan based on what comes up and what the other players do.

On top of all that, the cards and artwork are gorgeous and the components are top-notch. Compare this to a $20 Steve Jackson card game that's just a deck of average cards, and there's no comparison.

This is a ton of game in a small, easy-to-teach package, and everyone I've introduced it to -- from non-gamers to fairly hardcore gamers -- has enjoyed it. It's addictive, too!

---

March 2017: 18 plays over a 6-year period, at all player counts, winning and losing . . . and I've literally never had less than a fabulous time playing this. Re-rated from a 9 to a 10.

RATING: 7.5
The first time you play you'll probably have no idea how much to bid for cards, which I think is a common issue with auction games.  It's difficult to have a feel for the flow of the game and what cards are worth when you've never played.  But once you do this game really opens up as a highly engaging draft and auction game.  Each decision matters and bluffing can drive your opponents to overspend, which in turn reduces their ability to compete for cards that come afterward.

RATING: 9
8 - 01/11/2015 - Cool! I had been following this on internet reviews, and found very good comments. My first feelings after three games are equally positive. I like the quick turnover among player and the interaction throught the final auction. Although the drawing of cards is random, the auction potentially re-evaluates everything you did until there, but you must still play with strategy to acquire the right cards. Simple rules, solid mechanics, nice interaction among players, deep enough, from my experience it plays well with both two and three players.
9 - 18/04/2017 - I have played this also with four players. The game scales greatly keeping the same engagement and playing time with any numbers of players. My most recent games confirmed it is a good game for non-gamers and occasional players, and still fun for habitual players. With four players it becomes a bit more difficult to count others' card, and you lose a bit of control on your score, but it is still a very enjoyable experience.
