RATING: 8
[i]Biblios[/i] is by far my favorite 20-30 minute "filler" game.  While merely okay with four players and good with three, it is fantastic as a one-on-one game.

With two players, there are an abundance of opportunities for strategic bidding, bluffing, passing, and card dumping.  Many times during the auction phase, I have given up cards for gold from a color I was confident I would win with as little as a single card.  It is possible to fall behind during the drafting phase and come back to win if you are able to read the relative strength of your opponent's categories.  This is not as easy to accomplish in a 3-4 player game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game is so simple, but so clever.  The first phase allows for some really fun push-your-luck moments of trying to decide which cards to keep and which to hide in the auction, possibly giving your opponents even better cards.  The second phase is a pretty basic auction, but with some hidden-card bids to keep everyone guessing.  It's really hard to know how well you're doing until the end, especially with the random cards removed from the game.  Great little game overall.

RATING: 4
A fun little game, of auctions (and thus also groupthink) and card counting and risk taking.

Bit too short and volatile for me to care much about the outcome, which means that the rating suffers for me. But it's a really interesting game, the style of which was very new to me and thus felt very fresh.

I like it, somehow wish it had a bit more maybe? And a bit more granular scoring, which might dilute tension but give more feeling of control? I don't know. Also, I'd consider playing with trackable cards open, should make for a more tense affair I think, but ultimately this is pure preference. It's strange how I've turned around on the question of HTI, mostly because I now at least try to track, so it is painful to see the mistakes fellow players make when they don't in turn...

RATING: 8
The theme isn't especially fitting, as it's more of a stock market than something holy or Christian, but that's OK for a board game, I guess, since fun is supposed to be at the centre of one (at least in most cases). Although a lot of luck is implemented in this game, it is nonetheless - surprisingly - a very entertaining game which requires a little strategic thinking (but almost none) in order to try and win. When it's your turn, you pick up cards, whereby you can keep one of them. But it isn't as simple as that! When picking up those cards, you can only view them one at a time and you're forced to make the decision whether you should keep it, give it away to the players or for the auction. You choose how far you go. Will you take a moderate but nevertheless promising card for yourself or will you give it up in the hopes of getting a better one? As you can see, it is mostly luck and although in most cases I despise games which are made of pure luck, this is one exception which somehow manages to make me interested and extremely entertained… perhaps because the luck part isn't as obvious and seemingly hidden. Concerning the strategic part, two of five of the various categories have a best card with a value of four while the best card of the other three categories is only two. So often players will try to get the first two categories which are actually harder to get, which will attract most players and which aren't better at all than the other three categories. So you will be forced to select your focus which will determine your victory or failure.

Is coming out to be printed by a major publisher.

You are working to be majority in different classes. The majority at the end of the game earns the points. Sum the points, and you have your end score.

You take a card, choose a card for auction, and the rest pick a card. Once all cards are obtained, then the auction cards are sold after which the game scores are tallied.

Rendkívüli izgalommal álltam neki játszani, és mégsem csalódtam! Ketten játszottuk barátnőmmel, és annyira tetszett neki, hogy rögtön visszavágót kért, sőt azonnal kijelentette, hogy játszani akar még vele. Ezt még társas nem váltotta ki belőle (najó, talán a Ticket to Ride, az a kedvence).

Érzésre a játék hasonlít a Ticket to Ride-hoz (szett gyűjtés, titkos információk), ezért aki azt szereti, ezt is biztosan imádni fogja!
Blöffölés, kockáztatás, izgalom mind egy kis dobozban. De még milyen dobozban!!!
Alig várom, hogy többen is játsszuk!

RATING: 7
This is the game "For Sale" on steroids.  It layers in a bit more complexity into a familiar "two phase" game play.  It also offers players the ability to directly impact the scoring higher or lower via the dice modifiers.

Combine the gameplay with the game length and minimal setup time, and you have a winner.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Sharp, fast, interesting auction game with a few minor annoyances. The good stuff: the mechanism is really simple, easy to teach, and leads to some real drama later in the game as the cards go up for auction. Also, the art is great--even though it's basically an abstract card game the pictures of books being burned or talked up at the pulpit are great. -- The not-good: the current edition has absymally cheap thin cards. And the scoring mechanism is too minimalist--with the dice only inching up or down by a point, and only 5 opportunities for scoring, games can be decided by trivially low scores. I don't like games that have massive points inflation (where you're scoring regularly in triple digits), but having all that work go into such minuscule differences in outome isn't good either. (Basically, it needs to have the dice as multipliers on a base, not additive, so that small differences lead to wider disparities in results.) -- This is about 3/4ths of a truly brilliant game, but it's not quite there. I still like it, though.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
At first glance of this game i thought, oh is that it.. After loads of solid reviews i decided to go for it never the less..

The great thing about this game is the tension in the decisions you have to make every time you have that deck of cards in front of you.. And it still exciting and entertaining when its not your turn, watching other peoples faces as they draw the cards and think.. Oh shit i should've pushed my luck at little more ect.
This is a solid Small game that takes little time to play..

RATING: 6.6
主題:0.6
用中古世紀修道院收集各項宗教圖書(含禁書)來包裝的收集成套外加競標的遊戲，遊戲機制與主題勉強搭到一點點邊，畢竟成套收集可以套用很多主題(例如車子、珠寶..等)，只能說是個套用部相關主題的卡片競標遊戲!

美術:0.6
遊戲外盒的設計很有質感，卡片畫風有普普，沒有自己的特色(個人偏好有自己畫風的美工)，骰子不是用來骰的，而是用來翻轉，這一點出乎意料之外。

規則:0.8
規則簡單，好講解，遊戲時沒有太多爭議點，只是為什麼卡牌大小是要靠英文字的順序來比較，我覺得要是卡片針對同一種類分數的書，每張內容呈現書本不同的精緻度，來做為比較大小分數的依據，會更有帶入感!另外比較讓人困擾的一點就是宗教牌的進場發動時間，讓人小迷惑一會，簡單來說規則沒有太大的爭議點!帶新手完競標遊戲這一款很好入手，略比房地產拍賣高階一點!

設置:1
擺好圖板、骰子、卡片就可以開始玩，算是很方便!

路線:0.4 
算是走一步算一步的計算遊戲 見招拆招 遊戲中程才能比較明確自己的集牌路線。

互動:0.8 
互動性算高，有一點點針對性，當有人跟你湊同樣的牌時，就是考驗自己的決斷力，是要繼續博下去，還是要自己轉換路線，湊別種牌。

個人:0.6 假如湊牌類型可以其他不同主題的版本 本人可能會更加喜歡

朋友:0.6 大致反應還不錯 但僅僅不錯而已。

想玩:0.6 可能要等一陣子才會開來玩 做為小朋友的競標進階遊戲，還算是不錯的選擇。

收藏:0.6 外盒的很像書本，有閒錢可以收一下

總分:6.6
講評:湊牌過程中有一點點的小心機，可以快速多玩幾場，算是本遊戲的優點，就我而言，就像大老二一樣，玩的時候很刺激，但玩過後一點也回想不起來剛剛怎麼贏的。不像有些經典策略遊戲，會讓你玩過一場就印象深刻。

RATING: 8

The two phases are quite different, the gifting phase and then the auction phase, but both allow you to work towards creating a winning hand. RATING: 5
Biblios has its moments. When you raise a bid thinking another player will overbid and they do. When you raise a bid thinking another player will overbid and they don't. When you dump all your cards of a suit except one because every other player has seemingly dumped all theirs to auction for gold and you can win the suit with a single "1". Unfortunately said moments are too rare and only happen during the second half of the game; the first one being a draft-ish memory exercise where not a lot of interesting decisions happen and that can overstay its welcome at higher player counts. Globally, I'd say the game is very inoffensive: you're unlikely to have a bad time, you're unlikely to have a great time. But you'd probably rather play anything else you fancy.

It doesn't help that in the average game, dice values are irrelevant and it becomes a single matter of winning at an Euclidean division of 5 by the amount of players.

RATING: 5.5
Decent filler. People heralded this as a superior For Sale, but I was not crazy about this. I liked For Sale's art better, and I think I like auction mechanic more than blind draft too. That said, this game is possibly (probably?) deeper than For Sale at least... but I still like For Sale more because of the art mainly. (Yes, I know its shallow, but I don't grade fillers on their play as strongly). I think the push your luck draft isn't really phenomenal or anything - its okay, but it feels chancey, which I'm not crazy for. I've also lately been thinking that fillers should be less than 20 minutes ideally, and this approaches 30.

Plays: 3+

After about 10 or so plays of this, I find the game is a bit too light for my taste and Im not a fan of the push your luck. I dont like that some can draw in the 4s and such while others may keep drawing 1 golds or something. Id prefer more control and mitigation.

RATING: 5
Biblios is a set collection game with two parts to game play.  The first section is every player giving out 5 cards; one to themselves, one to the auction, and three to opposing players.  The second section is actually auctioning out the cards that were set apart in the beginning.  

At the end everyone compares the numbers they have collected from the five different collections and win points if they were the leader depending on the die corresponding to that set.  

The game is pretty simple with minimal amount of decisions to make during play.  I could play it again, but find 'For Sale' to have more decisions and also fit this time-frame.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
[b]Biblios[/b] was sold via auction 4/4/15. 
Received in a math trade 11/10/14.

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (6):[/COLOR]

[i]In the end, for my wife and I, this game didn't stand up to repeated play. Most of my plays were with 2 and I definitely think Biblios plays better with more, so I am quite surprised that it's so highly recommended for 2. The drafting of cards worked well with 2, but I found the dice manipulation to usually be a back and forth affair with very little difference in the numbers (most of our 2p games ended with a bunch of 3's and maybe a 2 and 4 thrown in). With 3 or 4 I t would gladly play it, but since it was mainly a 2p game I played with my wife I ended up trading it.

*I lowered my rating to a 6 based on the 2p experience, with 3 or 4 I would rate it an 8 and highly recommend playing it. [/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- An auction game that plays very well with 2
- An excellent cafe game [i](small footprint)[/i]
- Easy to teach since you can teach each phase of the game separately [i](drafting/auction phases) [/i]
- Interesting draft mechanic [i](you must choose a card for yourself, the auction piple and put cards out for the other players to choose)[/i].
- Dice manipulation: the whole game hinges on adjusting the value of the dice, the tricky part is when do you do it.[/i]

RATING: 7.5
心得:
禮物階段很有趣
不過能算的部分不少，但是一開始抽掉的牌讓推測性更不準 
可能要稍微記牌才能玩得好
規則:
*起始所有骰面 3，根據人數先平均棄不同幣值黃金牌，在暗抽棄對應數量牌
*遊戲先開始禮物階段，結束接競標階段，結束該按顏色牌數總合最高得骰子分數，平手比卡牌右下英文字母，最靠近A獲勝
1.禮物階段，由主動玩家抽(玩家數+1)張牌，一張一張抽，抽完就要決定放在哪，一張蓋著給自己，一張蓋著成為競標牌庫，其他開著，抽完給下面順位輪流拿，然後順時鐘換主動玩家
2.競標階段要洗牌，在由第一階段的起始玩家開始開競標牌庫，由主動玩家下家開始出價，建議用牌庫當作主動玩家指示物，競標只要pass就不能再加入
*標到不能付要逞罰， 其他玩家從該玩家手牌隨機抽一張，該競標牌重標，該玩家不能加入競標，緩合點的是隨機棄一張牌
*競標金幣卡出蓋著的卡牌張數，其它出金幣不找零
*最後分數平手比錢，在平手就看誰贏了monk骰(咖啡色)

RATING: 9
One of the best bidding/auction games. Sure, the theme may not fit AT ALL with the core mechanics, but Biblios plays so fast it's hard to naysay. Plus, it's a good decompression after big bloated 4x games or heavy Euros. It's tailor-made for variations and a slew of your own house rules: adding a fifth player, rolling all the die before you start (so they don't all start at 3), gifting one face down to your opponents, and extra punishments for overbidding on cards. Enjoyed by both veteran gamers and brand new players, Biblios is always a hoot.

RATING: 6
It’s a card collecting majorities game, competing to have the highest face value in each of 5 suits. The first half, establishing your starting hand, whizzes along. A turn here is to keep 1 card secretly, assign 1 to the auction pile secretly, and place 1 for each other player openly and watch what they take in clockwise order. The secrecy means there's enough hidden to ensure no one is quite sure exactly what suits people are aspiring to win. You can also claim gold cards, and once the deck is run through, these are used in the bidding phase, where each of the cards in the auction pile are now auctioned off, 1 at a time. This is where things become a bit more obvious about who's going for what. All the while, bishop interrupt cards are coming out which allow people to move the VP award for a suit of their choosing up or down by 1, also tipping hands. These tend to be pretty key and keenly fought over. If everyone fights, then things should net out pretty much the same, but if you let these go, you'll suddenly find that the suits you're collecting are worth much less than the others and you'll be out of it. The climax is the revelation at the end where all reveal, the suits are won, the VPs awarded and the game is won. There are too many secret cards to ever be sure about what your chances are, unless you go for overkill in a suit, but that means you won't likely win a second suit and you could be done over by someone who squeaks out wins in two suits and claims two lots of VPs. There’s enough randomness therefore for you to want to keep things pacey and fun, and means you don't want to take it too seriously, but there are probably too many auctions for a game that you don’t want to take too seriously. It therefore doesn't easily fall into a filler type category, but it's not weighty either. A mixed bag type of game, where you don't really feel like you've made interesting decisions, and that the cards you get kind of drift your way and then you hope things turn out well. Meaning there's not a lot of satisfaction at the end of it. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Sort of a step up from For Sale as it also features two phases.  The drafting (first) phase is interesting in that you have to draft a card, place one in the auction pile, and donate a card for each opponent to draft.  The kicker is that you draw one at a time and decide where to allocate each card as it appears.  So there is a push-your-luck element to the draft.  The auction phase has a nice dose of bluffing mixed with hand management as you sometimes will discard cards your opponents believe you are strong in to acquire extra gold.  You may end up dominating a color with far fewer influence points than they were calculating.  The only thing holding this game back is that the theme makes zero sense.  Just pretend it's a traditional card game.  It deserves it's status as an excellent filler and it does have a "Knizian" flare to it.

RATING: 6
Biblios is card game with two distinct parts.  In the first part, a player draws a number of cards sequentially and assigns them one-by-one to either himself, an offer for the other players to draft, or an auction pile to be distributed in the second half of the game.  Then in the second half of the game, players use money cards they acquired to buy cards in the auction pile (again, one-by-one).  The player having the greatest value of each of the colors of the game earns a number of points that starts at 3 but can be manipulated by in-game events.  So it's kind of like a partially-blind majority game with no points for runners up.  Some interesting ideas here, but ultimately it didn't do much for me.

(1 play)

It is a really engaging fun game of assuming, pushing your luck and then bidding and bluffing. 

Fun and Quick, almost impossible to play just once.

RATING: 4
My rating is for the game as a 2p, for which the game seems unbalanced bordering on broken. If you're playing 3p+, YMMV.

For 2p, you must randomly eliminate cards from the deck (you must do this to play fewer than the maximum number of participants, but for 2p, a lot of cards are removed) Because this card removal is random, there are so few of each card, that you often mostly or completely eliminate some suits, which degrades game play - sometimes substantially. Of 7 or 8 plays at 2p, three have been wonky and one was essentially broken. We stopped the game about 2/3 of the way through and looked through the card deck and found that one suit was completely missing. We tried designing a balanced 2p deck, but found that knowing which cards were in the relatively small play deck gave the game play an odd feel. We put it on a shelf a year or so ago with the intent of figuring out some house rules to fix things or simply to play with all the cards but modify scoring to keep the game from being too free with resources at a full card count, but in the interim have found other small filler 2p like Builders & Morels & Splendor & Aton... and so sold Biblios.

RATING: 6
decide
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Good, heavy filler where you play as monks, improving your monastery's library. Points are scored from five dice in different colors, placed on a minimal board. The player with the most points in each color get points equal to the dice current value.

The deck consists of differently valued cards in the five colors, money cards valued 1,2 and 3 and cards that raise or lower the values of the point dice.

The first round consists of a number of turns where the active player draws cards equal to number of players + 1. Each card is drawn separately and the player has to decide what to do with the card before drawing the next. The player has to keep one card, put one in the auction pile and place the rest face up on the table for the other players to share. Any dice manipulation cards are played immediately.

Then the other players in order picks one of the face up cards, the deck is passed to the next player who repeats the process until the deck runs out and each player has a hand of cards.

Then the auction takes place, where one card at a time is revealed from the auction pile. Players bid on the cards with the money on hand. If a money card is auctioned, players bid with colored cards with the player bidding the most cards winning. Cards spent this way are discarded face down so the other players can't track what colors now has fewer cards.

At the end of the game, the player with the highest total of points in a color gets that die, and the player with the highest total wins.

There are several things that make this game interesting:

Drawing one card at a time, without knowledge of all the cards you'll draw, adds quite a bit of tension.

Keeping track of who draws what is also important, since that allows you to decide what colors to go for. The totals for each color is known, so you can know whether or not you've collected enough points. But do you really need that last 2 or should you use it to raise your bid for a 3-gold card?

The dice manipulation allows you to lower the value of the color you watch your opponent collecting, reducing a possible gamewinner to nothing more than cards for bidding on money in the auction round.

RATING: 5
First play with 4 and my first impression is maybe there is too many secret and control issues for my taste.

Like an inverse of For Sale, plays in 2 phases: a draft followed by an auction. First issue could be overcome by having an idea of the deck distribution, as I didn't know what my chance was of drawing a good card in the draft, feeling very unlucky to put a single gold in the hand. However this uncertainty in compounded by 7 random cards removed at prep and only 3 of 5 cards drafted are revealed. The former I can cope with, the latter uncertainty increases with less players.

The bidding phase may reveal how much players are interested in a revealed card (drawn from a pile created from the draft) but again only if they are familiar with the deck. You are bidding to get a majority in any of the suits to claim that coloured die with the face up pip count as vps. Yet there are cards that can modify the values either up or down, so here is where I have a control issue especially if you have previously bidded hard for that colour only to have it changed. 

So either I have to play again with less or lighten up, but I felt I was playing a hybrid of High Society and Katzenjammer Blues which I feel both would provide more tension, theme and fairness in the time to play Biblios.

RATING: 4
I think this game works better with 3 than 4, but overall there are just so few scoring opportunities that the activity of playing this game easily feels futile. The way it works is you have a deck of cards. The active player takes 1, puts 1 face down for auction, then makes 1 available for each other player to take. Then the next player goes. At the end you auction off the auction pile. After the auction, whoever has the highest in numbers of one of the five colors, get somewhere between 1 and 6 points, depending on the end facing of a die that's been manipulated up and down over the course of the game. It's a cute idea, but the payoff at the end just feels disappointing.

:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:nostar: Re-playability

Played a few times, kicked to the curb, and I've never regretted it.

RATING: 9.997
One of the best fillers. I really don't have any complaints about this game. It could end up as a ten at some point.

Update: Obviously I have changed the rating to a 10. I also don't really like calling certain games filler games any more because if it is a good game it shouldn't need to have a specific classification.

For just a deck of cards and a few dice this game manages to include Auction/Card Drafting/Hand Management/Set Collection and Deduction all within a very short time. I don't think there are many others games that pack this big of a punch in such a small package.

Super easy to learn but also allows for gamers to excel.

RATING: 8.17
It's a double auction game (similar mechanic to For Sale).  The players first collect a hand of cards, then they use the hand of cards they collected as currency in the 2nd auction.  There is an element of set collection in this game and you can go for cards of various colors.  You can also manipulate how much each of those colors will be worth in the final scoring.  Good game.

Biblios works well as a 2P game which is a plus compared to For Sale.  However, the art work in For Sale is superior.

Both are great games.

RATING: 7.5
Description: Drafting, auction/bidding, set collection, hand management card game.
Players: 2 to 4, best with 4 or 3.  Light weight.
Designer: Steve Finn.  Publisher: IELLO.

Impression: Cool game that combines drafting in one phase and then auction/bidding for discards in the second phase. It greatly rewords planning and requires careful decision making. It's relatively easy and it could be considered a filler.

Likes: Drafting + Auction combined. Decision making and planning. Quick play. Nice components.

Dislikes: Low replayability.

RATING: 6
05-12-2014. Rated after 1 play. Fun drafting and auction game. 

The game first has a drafting an an auction part. In the drafting part, you first take 3 cards. Then you keep one, give one to your opponent and give one to a common pile. Afterwards you try to win the auctions for the cards in the pile. 

The players score points equal to the number of pips on the dice on a center board, if they control the most cards of that die color. Cards in the game let you manipulate those pips. Beware of the monks, those are the tie-breaker.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Biblios is a card game where players  play monks collecting different Books and relics for their monastery for points. Players first collect cards and disburse cards to other players getting a little clue about what  will be coming up in the auction phase. Then Players use the gifted cards to bid for cards in the public auction. The twist is  the person with the most cards of a certain type wins the points at which time the point value changes throughout the game. The game plays up to 4 players

Pros: Simple gameplay rules, fun auction mechanism, Fast gameplay, interaction with other players, nice card artwork

Cons: low player count

RATING: 2
One play, and it'll definitely be my last!  This is easily the worst game I've played this year - and I was surprised, as it has quite a good reputation.  The initial drafting mechanic seemed ok, and two of us saved cash, while the others collected sets.  But then, in the final draft, there was nothing for the two of us with money to buy, as only one colour came out, and cash - we both ended up with over 8 cash left over at the end of the game.  Then at final scoring, two players had gone deep into the same colour - one got 5 points, and the other nothing - but both had a huge amount in the colour.  In two of the others colours, one player won with just 3, just happening to have most, but as the other bonuses were all really low, it was pretty much irrelevant anyway!

RATING: 6
Quick card filler that keeps players guessing right until the very end. Ultimately there's just not enough control over he game to elevate this to anything more than a light filler with a groan factor. With cards removed from play you can't count, not that you really could effectively anyway because you don't know the primary cards other players have picked up, or what they've discarded in the auction for money. The effect is chaos where a six value suit at the end of the game can win and a nine value can lose - okay, that's okay, but it's not always obvious that'll be the case. Still, I'm perfectly happy to play as the rules are very light and easy to remember and the game keeps you engaged throughout.

RATING: 8

RATING: 7
Quick and elegant stock-market speculation game. Really like the dynamic where you toss out colors you give up on to bid for gold, so you can get the colors you want. It's fun to deduce which color is being tossed out by everybody, so you can get the cheap die. Definite homebrew quality to the artwork, but the cardstock is nice. The VHS box in which the 3rd edition is distributed is friggin' brilliant, making this the most portable game in my collection.

With 3-4 players, you get to see more cards, and what people pass up, to help with your deduction. With 2 players, bluffing plays a larger role, both with your donation, and in terms of driving up the price of a card you know your opponent wants.

This is the little, versatile game that can do anything. Good for 2, 3 or 4 players, playable in less than 30 minutes, easy to explain and ultra-portable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Played a PnP version with stamps instead of books. Biblios' gameplay is pretty simple, although I could never have guessed it from reading the rules alone. There is a strong push-your-luck aspect in both phases of the game. In the first phase, players have to decide which cards they will hold, put up for draft or auction without seeing the complete set. In the second phase, players bid for cards with very little knowledge on what cards are in the auction deck. Players can, however, assess the value of cards in relation to the importance to their collection, so there are some tactics to the seemingly random gameplay. Biblios is an above average filler which is fine for passing 20 minutes or so.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
#93 on my Top 100 Games of All Time (2017)
#72 on my Top 100 Games of All Time (2016)
#51 on my Top 100 Games of All Time (2015)

Great filler game! It's easy to pick up and understand. You go through a phase of drafting cards- each player draws cards off the deck equal to one more than the number of players. They give each player a card (including themselves) and put another in a discard pile. After the deck has been emptied, you then auction off the cards in the discard pile. You can purchase them with gold cards- assuming you kept any gold during the draft phase. Which you did, unless you have no idea what you're doing. Your goal is to collect the most of colored sets which will be equal to a certain number of points. Those point values all start at 3, but can be adjusted throughout the game as some cards are point modifiers.  

Acquired: June 2013 - Artscow

Small Card
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A drafting/trick taking/bidding game, in a stock market in a package with horrid graphics. Players are drafting cards (take one, put one in pile for bidding in second half of game,
‘ put one for every other player), in order to gain the most influence which in turn determines winning VPs according to the factions stock market value. 

Cards are multiuse and either provide gold for bidding, change the stock market, or give influence towards winning control. A clever twist is that influence cards can also be used to bid for gold cards. Players with the most VPs wins. Unfortunately, the stock market system is inelegant and overly static. The other parts of the games work well but I couldn’t help feel that the game was force fit together.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Very charming auction/set collection game that plays well even with 2. 

Played in 2 parts, the first is where the start player looks at cards up the the no. of players plus one. He then decides on each card if he wants to keep it, place it face down for auction, or leave it face up for other player to take. Certain cards in this phase and the following auction allow the owner to change the value of each colour die up, down or either.

Once the deck is plated through, the auction deck is shuffled and played through one at a time. Normal cards can be bid for using gold card acquired in the first phase. Gold cards have to be bid on using the normal cards.

At the end who ever has the highest value in each colour wins the points equal to the die. Most points wins. 

Really simple and smooth game-play makes this an ideal one to bring out with the family.

RATING: 8
Biblios is a simple, yet fun little card game that doesn't take much to learn, and can be played relatively quickly. It's played in two phases, the 'Gifting' Phase, where you give and take cards, and then the Auction Phase where you purchase cards with money and cards you accumulated in the first phase.

The game is extremely simple. But it just works. It's one of my all time favorite games.

RATING: 8
As a 2-player game, my rating goes down to a 5 or 6.

Biblios is way more fun with 3 or 4 people, good for a quick lunch break game with coworkers.  I like the surprise element, since so much is hidden from each player, and yet it it still rewards strategic moves (e.g. in retrospect I can usually pinpoint any mistakes I had made).  If you can't abide surprise losses, you might not like this game, but it's great for more social gamers who don't take losses very seriously but like a lot of interaction with other players and still enjoy some mental challenge.

RATING: 7.5
Played this twice and I'm very positive. Played it both times with 2 non-gamers and they enjoyed the game immensely. 

The setup time is nonexistent, except for the shuffling of the deck. Speaking of the deck, the only negative thing i can say about the game is the cards. I don't know if its the materials used or the thickness, but they are very stiff and that makes a riffleshuffle difficult to do. Also, there are a lot of cards in the game, which makes shuffling even more cumbersome.

Light and small games like this though, have a tendency to become samey after several plays. I'm not sure if this apllies to Biblios but we'll see in the future.


Update af 15 plays: It does get samey after several plays. Lowered my rating from 8 - 7. It's still a very good gateway'ish game with a small foot print and short playing time.

-------UPDATE-------------

Biblios is still a good game, but I don't play it very often. It a great gateway game but after a while the first half of the game (gift phase) is more or less an autopilot thing. I still love auctions though so the game is still going to stay in my collection.

RATING: 7
Great game for 3-4 players; not so much for 2 or 5 (latter via Steve Finn's variant). 
Combines elements of Poker, For Sale, and Dominion.  
We've adapted the designer's 5 Player variant (a 2nd set of dice for players coming in 2nd place in each category, along with pre-allocated gold cards) for playing with 3 or 4, and prefer to play that way.  
Unfortunately, even with Finn's variant,  there simply aren't enough cards to go around for 5 players.
And with 2 players, there aren't enough people to spread the risks/rewards of card randomness.

RATING: 6.5
A quick, fun game of set-collection and area-control (sort of)! It feels a lot like For Sale, but has some interesting twists -- a very clever partially secret card draft system, and the removal of random cards to handicap the card counters ... and I don't even like auctions very much! Should be easy to learn and work great as a filler! 

I LOVE the box (iello version)!

[b]--- Summary ---[/b]
The "board" shows 5 areas matching the card colors; each has a die with the 3-face on top. 

The deck is a mix of money cards (value 1-3); 5 colors (types of books), 2 of which have values 2-4 (each set sums to 25) and the other 3 which have values 1-2 (each set sums to 11); and several action cards (modify the final values of the 5 colors). For setup, remove a number -- based on the number playing -- of cards from the game (some specifically money, some totally random). 

Phase 1-- On your turn, you will draw n+1 cards, one by one. Of these, one will go to each player and one to the auction pile (face down): as you draw each card, must decide whether to take it yourself, put it in the auction pile, or place it face up on display (n-1 will be on display). After you've resolved the n+1 cards, the other players (in clockwise order) add a card from the display to their hand. Then the next player does the same. Repeat till you've distributed all cards in the deck.

Phase 2-- Shuffle the auction pile. On your turn reveal the top auction card. Starting with the next player clockwise, auction it off (round and round; if you pass you're out); bid/pay for money cards using a number of cards from your hand (winner removes these from game), bid/pay for all other cards with money cards. If you win with a  bid more than you can pay, lose a random card from your hand.

NOTE: in both Phases, the action cards (modifying the dice) are resolved as soon as you select the card, then the card is removed from the game.

After all cards auctioned off, for each color the player with the highest sum of cards (ties broken by letter on the cards; earliest in alphabetical order wins) earns the die of that color, worth VP shown on die face. The player with the most VP (tiebreaker = money cards still in hand) wins!

RATING: 10
Let me be absolutely clear about this--we've been playing Scripts and Scribes since its initial VHS box release--and we still play this at almost every other weekly game night...that's what 5 or 6 years, in a game group that is made up of hard-core, card game players, and boardgamers who thrive on playing a different game every week.  It is THAT good.

________________


Updated to a 10.  I honestly think this is quite possibly our most turned-to filler/short game.  It plays FANTASICALLY with 2, 3 or 4 players--not many games can acheive that tricky balance.  Fewer players is a slightly faster game, but at every level the game holds fun and tricky decisions that never sink to AP, because while tricky and hard to commit to, the decisions remain relatively simple, but rarely obvious.

This can be played with brnd new players, and they'll pick it up after a single run-through playing the two stages.  Only thing to watch to clarify is that the Bishop must be played when "chosen," that it can never be held in-hand, even though it can be placed into the auction.

This is a solid addition to the drafting genre of card games.  The less than perfect knowledge of the draft along with the ability to change values in the very streamlined scoring system makes it brilliant.  This may well be waiting to grow into a 10, and it is certainly a filler-length which will always be requested.  

This is the absolute, perfect filler-length 10.
We've now been playing it for a few years, and the desire to play it as a game night closer or a quick game with any number of players, 2,3,4 has not diminished AT ALL.

RATING: 8
Well, it turns out the small but rather rabid fan-base that this game has attracted are quite correct - this is truly an excellent little card game!  It's easy to learn, great fun to play, and makes you want to play several times in a row.  What I didn't expect was just how much this game would make me laugh.  For some reason I found some of the outrageous bids and unexpected turns of fortune to be quite hilarious!  The new edition of the game has some vastly improved artwork and pretty cool dice, although I do miss the old VCR case just a little bit!  However, 2-player games aren't as interesting, so the number of players is pretty much limited to 3 or 4.  It's nice that this game is more readily available now as it is one that holds a huge amount of appeal for hardcore gamers and non-gamers alike.  Yes, it turns out I can indeed love a strictly card game.  Game design: 4/5  Personal enjoyment: 4/5  Total: 8/10

RATING: 7
[Doctor Finn's 2007 (VHS) edition] {Arts, religion; auction, card-distributing, card-drafting; optimal 4p} I occasionally search for good games from small publishers.  Many people recommend Scripts and Scribes. So, I give it a try

Scripts & Scribes doesn't fail me.  It is really a nice game.  It is easy to teach and learn.  It is interactive and fun.  A typical game runs around 25-30 minutes.  It provides both strategy and tactical elements.  Due to the hidden information in donation phase, a player can create different intrigues to get points, waste other players' resources, etc.  The luck element is not as high as common card games.  Wise play really pays off.  In all, I enjoy playing this game!

The components are effective.  However, it is not that easy to distinguish different types of card in dim environment because the color tune is too dark.  The artwork doesn't interest me.  The cardstock is thick enough for many plays.

RATING: 7
Biblios is a clever game divided into two parts. In the first half you have to dole out cards to each player and one to the auction stack (for later). You can't look at them all first so there is a little bit of press-your-luck. Should I keep this first card which is pretty good, or should I risk it and hope that the next card is even better? I don't think I'm a big enough risk-taker to do well at this game. I always cave during the auction phase (part 2). I end up saving my cash for something really good, but that really good card never shows up. My terrible auction aptitude doesn't keep me from enjoying the game though.

RATING: 6
Light card game centred around collecting "books" as you attempt to compile a library. The cards come in five different categories and each turn the player has to decide between three choices 1). to keep a card 2). to give it to an opponent 3). to put it aside for a later auction. Victory points are awarded to the person who owns the greatest value of each card at the end of the game and the amount of points a category is worth can alter throughout the game through the playing of 'Church' cards. There's a small amount of strategy on offer here and some indirect conflict as you attempt to give opponents cards they don't want and reduce the victory points in the categories they're likely to win. Overall the game is a bit too thin, although it does play quickly and has an element of tension when the victory points are being calculated as it is often difficult to know who has won until right at the end.

Update: Played again and is much better now we're playing it correctly and I know what I'm doing! :) Surprising how much the imperfect information comes into effect, even with only 2 players. It is a pretty subtle game and takes a few plays to really wrap your head around how to play well.

RATING: 6
I was a bit disappointed in Biblios. I love the card-drafting mechanic (although luck plays a huge part ... I saw only one "3" money card in my first game) and the auctions are fine. My disappointment comes with the very limited opportunities to change the values of the categories, and the fact that the game almost seems over in terms of what you can influence before the auction phase even starts. There are only eight cards that change the category values, and in our three-player game, two were randomly not in the game. Two or three more came out in the drafting phase so early that nobody really had any idea what values they wanted to raise or lower (not really having a stake in any of the categories yet). The last card or two came out very early in the auction, so for the last half of the game - almost the entire auction phase - there was no way to adjust the values of the categories. By then, I knew I was going to win a "3" and a ""4" value category for 7 points. All the other categories were locked in a "4" value, so in a three-player game someone was guaranteed to win at least two categories for 8 points. Which is a long-winded way of explaining that for half the game, I was just playing out the string with no way to change anything that mattered (of course, I didn't know this for sure, and found out only after the game that two of the eight value-adjustor cards were out). OK, it's a card game and that will have some hands that are skewed from time to time. I understand that. But I really didn't feel I could influence much once the drafting was done, and being lucky enough to see the high-value cards on your turn in the draft is really what the game boils down to, rather than the anti-climactic auction. Biblios is light and I'd certainly try it again, but it felt to me like a Knizia filler on par with Quandry but without the balance and surprisingly deep player options Knizia seems to infuse into his filler games.

RATING: 6
:thumbsup: A drafting/bluffing/auction game that works great with 2.
:thumbsup: Creates some mind games between you and your opponent.
[b][color=green]------------------------------[/color][/b]
:?block: There is a memory component, but we found it to be insignificant. It's more about knowing the general direction your opponent is going in, and not every single card you know they ever had. The reason is that players often strategically discard some of their cards in the auction phase, face down, and it greatly diminishes the benefit of trying to remember every card you gave them in the drafting phase. Rather, you're trying to read your opponent based on their betting and category value manipulation.
[b][color=red]------------------------------[/color][/b]
:thumbsdown: The ratio of what's happening on the table and in your head is heavily skewed towards the latter. There's no immediate resolution, and it can feel like the whole game is one gigantic turn setting up the final scoring. This somehow makes the game feel heavier than it is.
:thumbsdown: There's not much theme here. For one, we never call categories Monks/Pigments/Holy Books/etc., but rather just brown/blue/green/etc. They are just different categories for set collection, and they don't behave in any remarkable way that would give them any distinction or character.

RATING: 8
It is currently one of my most played games.  Good tension and little downtime.

Compact and has a very small footprint, so it travels well.

Scales well from 2-4.

Great for gamers and non-gamers.  It can be taught and played in a short amount of time.

I really do not like the artwork or theme. Though I like original themes, I just don't like this one.  I think a theme that had more to do with set collection would rest more easily with the mechanics of this one and therefore be more evocotive.

The reprint will likely appeal to me more, so when I where out this version I'll be happy to buy the new one.

Like For Sale, Coloretto, No Thanks and a few others I think this one belongs in every collection.  Easy to teach and fun for all. 



Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 5
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 4
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 3
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 4.5

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An essential addition to every game library,  this entry offers some truly unique game play with a high replay value.

The game itself,  has two distinct phases that compliment each other in perfect unison.  The first phase is a refreshingly unique mechanic, and to me,  is the highlight of the game.  It is rife with harrowing choices and unlike anything I have ever experienced before.

As far as the ideal player count is concerned,  it's a much trickier proposition than it appears.  This is mostly due to the fact that there are so few victory points available in the game - and this creates the only flaw,  in an otherwise perfect design.  The thing is,  the mechanics of the game are at their stellar best when this is played multi-player.  However,  with so few points to go around,  all players need to be on board,  as any sub-optimal play can skew things in a detrimental way - and that is a lot to ask of every player,  every turn,  in a game of this weight.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Fantastic! I'm really impressed by this card game. I've played it four times now and am eager to get a copy when it's finally reprinted. I named it my favorite card game of 2008, but it's more than that, it was a real contender for my favorite game period of 2008. This game looks unassuming and ordinary. It wasn't on my radar whatsoever until a friend got a copy and suggested playing. It's now one of my favorite card games ever. I've always liked, but not loved, card games like Lost Cities, Odin's Ravens, and Balloon Cup. They're a good idea, but not quite satisfying. The idea of a unique and novel card game with staying power to play in 20 minutes with your significant other has proven elusive. I've ended up turning to small board games in order to get enough decision-making to be satisfying in that time frame, such as Aton, Hey That's My Fish, and Fjords, but Scripts & Scribes is a card game with decision-making and tension galore. I won't go into great detail, but essentially you're trying to get the majority of cards in various colors, and each turn you draw three cards, allocating one to yourself, one to your opponent, and one to a common pool that will be auctioned off at the end of the game. You draw the three cards one at a time, making the decision of where to allocate before seeing the rest of the three, which makes it a tense and agonizing decision. I highly recommend this card game for anyone who has enjoyed the Kosmos line, but hasn't found them to pack quite enough of a punch.

Purchased: November 21, 2010

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
I played Biblios Dice before Biblios, despite the former predating the latter by several years, so my impression of this was shaped by my experience with the dice version. They're very similar games with just a few important differences.

You're still competing to have a majority in a color to claim the points for a particular die, which is variable depending on how many pips are shown on the die. And you're still collecting money to compete in auctions. What I liked about this version over the dice version was that it seemed much quicker. What I didn't like was that the competition for control of a color was all or nothing, so you lost a lot of the nuances of Biblios Dice where you might be contented taking second place in several contests. I also found the auction mechanism in the dice version more interesting.

Overall, Biblios is very quick... but even so, I didn't find the game compelling for the amount of time you invest in it. Someone compared it to For Sale... I'd much rather play FS than this.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The game works pretty smoothly. In first phase, players get cards: in every turn, you choose one card for yourself, one for auction (the second phase) and which to give to the other players. The thing is that you [b]only look one at a time[/b]. So you have to estimate and sometimes hope for the best. It is pretty fun to see someone take for himself the first card, only to "oh, no" once the second, third or fourth come along. Bishop cards (the ones that change the value of the dice) must be used immediately.

The firs phase ends when the deck ends. Then starts the second phase - the auction phase. All the cards put for auction in the first phase will the sold. For resources cards the players pay with gold, for gold cards, the players pay with cards.

Once the second phase ends, players count the number of resources they have for each type, and the one with the most, take the resource die linked to that resource, scoring the amount of points shown in the dice. The winner is the player with the most points.

[thing=34219][/thing] is a really fun filler. It has interaction and decisions throughout the whole play. Sure, luck plays a big part, but the game is short enough for this doesn't bother too much, and usually smart play is more important.

The quality of the components is good, though nothing major. 

My review (in portuguese) is [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/869294/biblios-resenha-em-portugues-review-in-portugues]here[/url].
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
I am not a big fan of the theme, but everyone seems to love this game.  It is always easy to throw it out there at 12:30am and get a quick game in before calling it a night.  Never too late or tired for Biblios.  

I would actually rate this game a 9 or 10, if it were not for the quality of the cards.  They do not shuffle well, because they stick together. The card edges get dinged up fast exposing the white under the black.  Thus you can, if you are observant, realize what some cards are because of marks left. But this won't last long since many will be like this after about 5+ plays.  The cards are also glossy with a laminate sheen, so if you are germ-a-phobic the fingerprints and oil from peoples hands is very visible.  

Don't let all of this deter you however, this is a GREAT game, and all gamers should own it.  In the end I hope more simple fun drafting/bidding games like this one come around, and preferably with a cooler theme.

RATING: 7
There is a palpable sense of tension and a fair amount of second guessing during gameplay. I am constantly wondering the right balance of taking gold cards or score cards. While there is some luck in card draw, choosing which cards to keep and which cards to go public is crucial and likely requires repeated plays to get a better feel. The auction part is quite standard, but the dual currency during auction requires a delicate balancing act. Not enough cash and you can't buy more cards, but it is tough to let go of cards to get more cash. Tough, tough decisions.
The only gripe I have is the final scoring. There aren't many ways to score and also many ways to modulate the final score. This makes it tough to change strategy mid-way...something I like to do in games.

RATING: 7
very easy to learn and quick gameplay. First there is like a "market phase" where everyone can pick cards and accumulate a stack of cards. In the second phase there is an auction for every card. You try to collect the most points in certain colors which are "rated" with dice. The higher dice value shown, the more points the color is worth. That results in a competition for the most wanted colors, except someone alters those dice with special cards which can be very valuable and make the game very very more interesting.
Overall I enjoyed it pretty much to play this game. Played it with 4 players.

Exciting for someone else, apparantly, but dull for me.

RATING: 7
VERY cool.  It's a little more than your typical filler game, and it's a neat mesh of Money! and For Sale.  The first half of the game is setting up your hand, other players' hands, and the auction pile; the second half of the game is bidding on the cards in the auction pile with cards out of your hand.  This is a nifty little game with a couple of different strategies for accumulating hand cards, and that you determine points off of a separate, relative board is what elevates this to another level.  I can see this becoming my next new filler game.

1 play: 2 players

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
You are an abbot of a medieval monastery competing with other abbots to amass the greatest library of sacred books. To do so, you need to have both the workers and resources to run a well-functioning scriptorium. To acquire workers and resources, you use a limited supply of donated gold. In addition, you must be on good terms with the powerful bishop, who can help you in your quest.
\13\\13\
The object of the game is to score the most Victory Points. You win Victory Points by winning any of the 5 categories: Illuminators, Scribes, Manuscripts, Scrolls, and Supplies. You win a category by having the highest total number of workers (Scribes, Illuminators) or resources (Manuscripts, Scrolls, Supplies) in that category. This is determined by the numbers in the upper left corner on the cards. At the start of the game, each category is worth 3 Victory Points. As the game progresses, the values on the Value Board will change and some categories will become worth more or less Victory Points than others. The game is divided into 2 stages: a Donation stage and an Auction stage. During the Donation stage, players acquire free cards according to an established plan. In the Auction stage, players purchase cards in auction rounds. After the two stages, winners of each category are determined and Victory Points awarded. The player with the most Victory Points wins.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Here's a BGG rarity, a game that actually lives up to the hype. It has a very unique drafting mechanism tied to an equally unique set collection mechanism. The cards you are trying to collect are a bit of a moving target, because the other players are not only competing for the same sets, but also directly controlling the value of each set for the end game scoring. It ends up being a very cool interlocking puzzle with multiple approaches to winning. Do I focus on driving the value down on a color I am weak in? Do I let my opponent control the market values and hope his decisions telegraph his intentions, so that I can counter them? The depth of the game is impressive, considering I can teach someone to play in literally five minutes.

RATING: 8
This is a fairly fast game and it is a lot of fun to play. There are two phases to the game. In the first players take turn selecting cards to keep, offer to the other players or place into the auction for later. In the second phase the cards from the auction pile are auctioned off, and in the end whoever has collected the most cards of each color gets that die, and the score is based on the pips on each die. I honestly have not been able to figure out a good strategy to win but I enjoy trying. 1-11-16

RATING: 8
Definitely a surprise hit/hidden gem. 

I've had this on my Wishlist for years. Probably since 2010ish when a reprint/retheme triggered some buzz at BGG.con. While it was on my list to track down and play, it was never high enough to be a priority. 

Perhaps based entirely on my low expectations, I found this surprisingly enjoyable. The "gift" phase was a fun exercise in "push your luck" as you tried to determine what to keep, what to auction, and what to give up. The second phase of the game is a nice auction that seemed to work relatively well even with 2P. 

While the theme was clearly pasted on, the artwork was fine and the game flew by. Our 2P game seemed to be under 25m including a code rules reading/explanation. This feels very similar to something like Sushi Go - while it's not itself an amazing/groundbreaking game, it fulfills it's role of a light filler game exceptionally well. There are some similarities between this and For Sale. 

My rating may go up or down with additional plays. For what it does:

:star::star::star::star::nostar:

RATING: 7
Interesting 2 stage game. The 1st stage is to build your hand. You draw 3 cards (1 at a time) and assign to 3 areas (your hand, the auction pile, common area). Each other player takes a card from the common pile. After you have gone through the deck. The auction of the auction pile takes place. You bid gold for color cards and cards for gold cards. Very interesting game.

RATING: 8
Excellent filler card game! Clever mechanics. Plays very smoothly, with interesting decisions but avoids being a brain-burner. Very portable so you can easily carry it around if you want. This has taken "Mystery Rummy's" place as the always-willing-to-play card game for my wife and I.

I find this game best with two. With two it is possible to work out close approximations of what your opponent has, so the bluffing and bidding become extremely tense.

The artwork is pretty ugly, and I'm not sure why the card value distributions for the workers vs. the resources are different, but the game itself is a lot of fun! An excellent self-published game.

RATING: 6.8
This is an absolutely excellent filler game. Probably the best filler game that I've ever played right next to splendor. My wife loves this game because of it simplicity and creative card play. I would never turn down a game of Biblios!  It is excellent!  I love the push your luck aspect of the game when you have to draw the three cards in a two player game and decide what to do as you draw them one by one. I also love how you never know for sure what your opponent has in their hand but you have a decent idea because you've been giving them a fair amount of cards yourself. It's always exciting and intense when you finally show what cards you have at the end of the game determine who wins the dice for points and ultimately who wins the game.

Note:  Sleeved with Fantasy Flight Standard Gray Pack (blue backing)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game uses a clever assign / auction mechanic that adds a unique twist to set collection.  I was concerned at first that the auction would not be exciting with only two people; however, this was not the case.  The limited resources along with the angst of the unknown add tension to the auction that makes each one meaningful.  Assigning cards to the three different piles and the ability to manipulate the VPs via the Bishops (Cookie Jar) allows for some subtle bluffing techniques.  This is a great little game that plays fast.  My wife and I played two games with rules explanation in less than 45 minutes. 
 
The current availability of the game is a deterrent.  It is currently out of print and copies are being offered at a high value.  There is a reprint in the works that should be available soon.  That should make this great game more affordable and more accessible.

RATING: 6
Biblios proved itself a very solid game. It looks good, is very easy to teach and learn, and plays at a good clip. The game has you cringing at tough decisions and bad luck, while hooting, and laughing when things work out your way.

Yet, it's mostly a bit one sided. As if the rest of the table isn't in on the joke, or why you have such a hard time deciding what to do. Contrast this with a game like The Boss, where every decision, and bluff is more overt, and Biblios feels more like back-room wheeling and dealing.

I'm not sure yet where my rating will end up, but my friends really enjoyed it, which is a plus.

RATING: 7
This game is slowly growing on me. I initially bought it for the theme and the artwork (hey it looked cool). After several plays however I felt it was far too luck driven. I sort of set it aside and didn't play it very much. Lately however I have played a few games of it and actually saw some aspects of the gameplay that I hadn't seen before. I have since upped my rating and have decided to mark this one: Final Verdict Pending.
